As it is evident that my people have\r","advised me wrongly, I will not cast you three people into the dreadful\r","Garden of the Clinging Vines; but your animals must be driven into the\r","Black Pit in the mountain, for my subjects cannot bear to have them\r","around.\"\r","\r","The Wizard was so pleased to have saved the two children and himself\r","that he said nothing against this decree; but when the Princess had gone\r","both Jim and Eureka protested they did not want to go to the Black Pit,\r","and Dorothy promised she would do all that she could to save them from\r","such a fate.\r","\r","For two or three days after this--if we call days the periods between\r","sleep, there being no night to divide the hours into days--our friends\r","were not disturbed in any way. They were even permitted to occupy the\r","House of the Sorcerer in peace, as if it had been their own, and to\r","wander in the gardens in search of food.\r","\r","Once they came near to the enclosed Garden of the Clinging Vines, and\r","walking high into the air looked down upon it with much interest. They\r","saw a mass of tough green vines all matted together and writhing and\r","twisting around like a nest of great snakes. Everything the vines\r","touched they crushed, and our adventurers were indeed thankful to have\r","escaped being cast among them.\r","\r","Whenever the Wizard went to sleep he would take the nine tiny piglets\r","from his pocket and let them run around on the floor of his room to\r","amuse themselves and get some exercise; and one time they found his\r","glass door ajar and wandered into the hall and then into the bottom part\r","of the great dome, walking through the air as easily as Eureka could.\r","They knew the kitten, by this time, so they scampered over to where she\r","lay beside Jim and commenced to frisk and play with her.\r","\r","The cab-horse, who never slept long at a time, sat upon his haunches and\r","watched the tiny piglets and the kitten with much approval.\r","\r","\"Don't be rough!\" he would call out, if Eureka knocked over one of the\r","round, fat piglets with her paw; but the pigs never minded, and enjoyed\r","the sport very greatly.\r","\r","Suddenly they looked up to find the room filled with the silent,\r","solemn-eyed Mangaboos. Each of the vegetable folks bore a branch covered\r","with sharp thorns, which was thrust defiantly toward the horse, the\r","kitten and the piglets.\r","\r","\"Here--stop this foolishness!\" Jim roared, angrily; but after being\r","pricked once or twice he got upon his four legs and kept out of the way\r","of the thorns.\r","\r","The Mangaboos surrounded them in solid ranks, but left an opening to the\r","doorway of the hall; so the animals slowly retreated until they were\r","driven from the room and out upon the street. Here were more of the\r","vegetable people with thorns, and silently they urged the now frightened\r","creatures down the street. Jim had to be careful not to step upon the\r","tiny piglets, who scampered under his feet grunting and squealing, while\r","Eureka, snarling and biting at the thorns pushed toward her, also tried\r","to protect the pretty little things from injury. Slowly but steadily the\r","heartless Mangaboos drove them on, until they had passed through the\r","city and the gardens and come to the broad plains leading to the\r","mountain.\r","\r","\"What does all this mean, anyhow?\" asked the horse, jumping to escape a\r","thorn.\r","\r","\"Why, they are driving us toward the Black Pit, into which they\r","threatened to cast us,\" replied the kitten. \"If I were as big as you\r","are, Jim, I'd fight these miserable turnip-roots!\"\r","\r","\"What would you do?\" enquired Jim.\r","\r","\"I'd kick out with those long legs and iron-shod hoofs.\"\r","\r","\"All right,\" said the horse; \"I'll do it.\"\r","\r","An instant later he suddenly backed toward the crowd of Mangaboos and\r","kicked out his hind legs as hard as he could. A dozen of them smashed\r","together and tumbled to the ground, and seeing his success Jim kicked\r","again and again, charging into the vegetable crowd, knocking them in\r","all directions and sending the others scattering to escape his iron\r","heels. Eureka helped him by flying into the faces of the enemy and\r","scratching and biting furiously, and the kitten ruined so many vegetable\r","complexions that the Mangaboos feared her as much as they did the horse.\r","\r","But the foes were too many to be repulsed for long. They tired Jim and\r","Eureka out, and although the field of battle was thickly covered with\r","mashed and disabled Mangaboos, our animal friends had to give up at last\r","and allow themselves to be driven to the mountain.\r","\r","[Illustration]\r","\r","\r","\r","\r","CHAPTER 7.\r","\r","INTO THE BLACK PIT AND OUT AGAIN\r","\r","\r","When they came to the mountain it proved to be a rugged, towering chunk\r","of deep green glass, and looked dismal and forbidding in the extreme.\r","Half way up the steep was a yawning cave, black as night beyond the\r","point where the rainbow rays of the colored suns reached into it.\r","\r","The Mangaboos drove the horse and the kitten and the piglets into this\r","dark hole and then, having pushed the buggy in after them--for it seemed\r","some of them had dragged it all the way from the domed hall--they began\r","to pile big glass rocks within the entrance, so that the prisoners could\r","not get out again.\r","\r","\"This is dreadful!\" groaned Jim. \"It will be about the end of our\r","adventures, I guess.\"\r","\r","\"If the Wizard was here,\" said one of the piglets, sobbing bitterly, \"he\r","would not see us suffer so.\"\r","\r","\"We ought to have called him and Dorothy when we were first attacked,\"\r","added Eureka. \"But never mind; be brave, my friends, and I will go and\r","tell our masters where you are, and get them to come to your rescue.\"\r","\r","The mouth of the hole was nearly filled up now, but the kitten gave a\r","leap through the remaining opening and at once scampered up into the\r","air. The Mangaboos saw her escape, and several of them caught up their\r","thorns and gave chase, mounting through the air after her. Eureka,\r","however, was lighter than the Mangaboos, and while they could mount only\r","about a hundred feet above the earth the kitten found she could go\r","nearly two hundred feet. So she ran along over their heads until she had\r","left them far behind and below and had come to the city and the House of\r","the Sorcerer. There she entered in at Dorothy's window in the dome and\r","aroused her from her sleep.\r","\r","As soon as the little girl knew what had happened she awakened the\r","Wizard and Zeb, and at once preparations were made to go to the rescue\r","of Jim and the piglets. The Wizard carried his satchel, which was quite\r","heavy, and Zeb carried the two lanterns and the oil can. Dorothy's\r","wicker suit-case was still under the seat of the buggy, and by good\r","fortune the boy had also placed the harness in the buggy when he had\r","taken it off from Jim to let the horse lie down and rest. So there was\r","nothing for the girl to carry but the kitten, which she held close to\r","her bosom and tried to comfort, for its little heart was still beating\r","rapidly.\r","\r","Some of the Mangaboos discovered them as soon as they left the House of\r","the Sorcerer; but when they started toward the mountain the vegetable\r","people allowed them to proceed without interference, yet followed in a\r","crowd behind them so that they could not go back again.\r","\r","Before long they neared the Black Pit, where a busy swarm of Mangaboos,\r","headed by their Princess, was engaged in piling up glass rocks before\r","the entrance.\r","\r","\"Stop, I command you!\" cried the Wizard, in an angry tone, and at once\r","began pulling down the rocks to liberate Jim and the piglets. Instead of\r","opposing him in this they stood back in silence until he had made a\r","good-sized hole in the barrier, when by order of the Princess they all\r","sprang forward and thrust out their sharp thorns.\r","\r","[Illustration: THROUGH THE BLACK PIT.]\r","\r","Dorothy hopped inside the opening to escape being pricked, and Zeb and\r","the Wizard, after enduring a few stabs from the thorns, were glad to\r","follow her. At once the Mangaboos began piling up the rocks of glass\r","again, and as the little man realized that they were all about to be\r","entombed in the mountain he said to the children:\r","\r","\"My dears, what shall we do? Jump out and fight?\"\r","\r","\"What's the use?\" replied Dorothy. \"I'd as soon die here as live much\r","longer among those cruel and heartless people.\"\r","\r","\"That's the way I feel about it,\" remarked Zeb, rubbing his wounds.\r","\"I've had enough of the Mangaboos.\"\r","\r","\"All right,\" said the Wizard; \"I'm with you, whatever you decide. But we\r","can't live long in this cavern, that's certain.\"\r","\r","Noticing that the light was growing dim he picked up his nine piglets,\r","patted each one lovingly on its fat little head, and placed them\r","carefully in his inside pocket.\r","\r","Zeb struck a match and lighted one of the lanterns. The rays of the\r","colored suns were now shut out from them forever, for the last chinks\r","had been filled up in the wall that separated their prison from the Land\r","of the Mangaboos.\r","\r","\"How big is this hole?\" asked Dorothy.\r","\r","\"I'll explore it and see,\" replied the boy.\r","\r","So he carried the lantern back for quite a distance, while Dorothy and\r","the Wizard followed at his side. The cavern did not come to an end, as\r","they had expected it would, but slanted upward through the great glass\r","mountain, running in a direction that promised to lead them to the side\r","opposite the Mangaboo country.\r","\r","\"It isn't a bad road,\" observed the Wizard, \"and if we followed it it\r","might lead us to some place that is more comfortable than this black\r","pocket we are now in. I suppose the vegetable folk were always afraid to\r","enter this cavern because it is dark; but we have our lanterns to light\r","the way, so I propose that we start out and discover where this tunnel\r","in the mountain leads to.\"\r","\r","The others agreed readily to this sensible suggestion, and at once the\r","boy began to harness Jim to the buggy. When all was in readiness the\r","three took their seats in the buggy and Jim started cautiously along the\r","way, Zeb driving while the Wizard and Dorothy each held a lighted\r","lantern so the horse could see where to go.\r","\r","Sometimes the tunnel was so narrow that the wheels of the buggy grazed\r","the sides; then it would broaden out as wide as a street; but the floor\r","was usually smooth, and for a long time they travelled on without any\r","accident. Jim stopped sometimes to rest, for the climb was rather steep\r","and tiresome.\r","\r","\"We must be nearly as high as the six colored suns, by this time,\" said\r","Dorothy. \"I didn't know this mountain was so tall.\"\r","\r","\"We are certainly a good distance away from the Land of the Mangaboos,\"\r","added Zeb; \"for we have slanted away from it ever since we started.\"\r","\r","But they kept steadily moving, and just as Jim was about tired out with\r","his long journey the way suddenly grew lighter, and Zeb put out the\r","lanterns to save the oil.\r","\r","To their joy they found it was a white light that now greeted them, for\r","all were weary of the colored rainbow lights which, after a time, had\r","made their eyes ache with their constantly shifting rays. The sides of\r","the tunnel showed before them like the inside of a long spy-glass, and\r","the floor became more level. Jim hastened his lagging steps at this\r","assurance of a quick relief from the dark passage, and in a few moments\r","more they had emerged from the mountain and found themselves face to\r","face with a new and charming country.\r","\r","[Illustration]\r","\r","\r","\r","\r","CHAPTER 8.\r","\r","THE VALLEY OF VOICES\r","\r","\r","By journeying through the glass mountain they had reached a delightful\r","valley that was shaped like the hollow of a great cup, with another\r","rugged mountain showing on the other side of it, and soft and pretty\r","green hills at the ends. It was all laid out into lovely lawns and\r","gardens, with pebble paths leading through them and groves of beautiful\r","and stately trees dotting the landscape here and there. There were\r","orchards, too, bearing luscious fruits that are all unknown in our\r","world. Alluring brooks of crystal water flowed sparkling between their\r","flower-strewn banks, while scattered over the valley were dozens of the\r","quaintest and most picturesque cottages our travelers had ever beheld.\r","None of them were in clusters, such as villages or towns, but each had\r","ample grounds of its own, with orchards and gardens surrounding it.\r","\r","As the new arrivals gazed upon this exquisite scene they were enraptured\r","by its beauties and the fragrance that permeated the soft air, which\r","they breathed so gratefully after the confined atmosphere of the tunnel.\r","Several minutes were consumed in silent admiration before they noticed\r","two very singular and unusual facts about this valley. One was that it\r","was lighted from some unseen source; for no sun or moon was in the\r","arched blue sky, although every object was flooded with a clear and\r","perfect light. The second and even more singular fact was the absence of\r","any inhabitant of this splendid place. From their elevated position they\r","could overlook the entire valley, but not a single moving object could\r","they see. All appeared mysteriously deserted.\r","\r","The mountain on this side was not glass, but made of a stone similar to\r","granite. With some difficulty and danger Jim drew the buggy over the\r","loose rocks until he reached the green lawns below, where the paths and\r","orchards and gardens began. The nearest cottage was still some distance\r","away.\r","\r","\"Isn't it fine?\" cried Dorothy, in a joyous voice, as she sprang out of\r","the buggy and let Eureka run frolicking over the velvety grass.\r","\r","\"Yes, indeed!\" answered Zeb. \"We were lucky to get away from those\r","dreadful vegetable people.\"\r","\r","\"It wouldn't be so bad,\" remarked the Wizard, gazing around him, \"if we\r","were obliged to live here always. We couldn't find a prettier place, I'm\r","sure.\"\r","\r","He took the piglets from his pocket and let them run on the grass, and\r","Jim tasted a mouthful of the green blades and declared he was very\r","contented in his new surroundings.\r","\r","\"We can't walk in the air here, though,\" called Eureka, who had tried it\r","and failed; but the others were satisfied to walk on the ground, and the\r","Wizard said they must be nearer the surface of the earth than they had\r","been in the Mangaboo country, for everything was more homelike and\r","natural.\r","\r","\"But where are the people?\" asked Dorothy.\r","\r","The little man shook his bald head.\r","\r","\"Can't imagine, my dear,\" he replied.\r","\r","They heard the sudden twittering of a bird, but could not find the\r","creature anywhere. Slowly they walked along the path toward the nearest\r","cottage, the piglets racing and gambolling beside them and Jim pausing\r","at every step for another mouthful of grass.\r","\r","Presently they came to a low plant which had broad, spreading leaves, in\r","the center of which grew a single fruit about as large as a peach. The\r","fruit was so daintily colored and so fragrant, and looked so appetizing\r","and delicious that Dorothy stopped and exclaimed:\r","\r","\"What is it, do you s'pose?\"\r","\r","The piglets had smelled the fruit quickly, and before the girl could\r","reach out her hand to pluck it every one of the nine tiny ones had\r","rushed in and commenced to devour it with great eagerness.\r","\r","\"It's good, anyway,\" said Zeb, \"or those little rascals wouldn't have\r","gobbled it up so greedily.\"\r","\r","\"Where are they?\" asked Dorothy, in astonishment.\r","\r","They all looked around, but the piglets had disappeared.\r","\r","\"Dear me!\" cried the Wizard; \"they must have run away. But I didn't see\r","them go; did you?\"\r","\r","\"No!\" replied the boy and the girl, together.\r","\r","\"Here,--piggy, piggy, piggy!\" called their master, anxiously.\r","\r","Several squeals and grunts were instantly heard at his feet, but the\r","Wizard could not discover a single piglet.\r","\r","\"Where are you?\" he asked.\r","\r","\"Why, right beside you,\" spoke a tiny voice. \"Can't you see us?\"\r","\r","[Illustration: \"ARE THERE REALLY PEOPLE IN THIS ROOM?\"]\r","\r","\"No,\" answered the little man, in a puzzled tone.\r","\r","\"We can see you,\" said another of the piglets.\r","\r","The Wizard stooped down and put out his hand, and at once felt the small\r","fat body of one of his pets. He picked it up, but could not see what he\r","held.\r","\r","\"It is very strange,\" said he, soberly. \"The piglets have become\r","invisible, in some curious way.\"\r","\r","\"I'll bet it's because they ate that peach!\" cried the kitten.\r","\r","\"It wasn't a peach, Eureka,\" said Dorothy. \"I only hope it wasn't\r","poison.\"\r","\r","\"It was fine, Dorothy,\" called one of the piglets.\r","\r","\"We'll eat all we can find of them,\" said another.\r","\r","\"But _we_ mus'n't eat them,\" the Wizard warned the children, \"or we too\r","may become invisible, and lose each other. If we come across another of\r","the strange fruit we must avoid it.\"\r","\r","Calling the piglets to him he picked them all up, one by one, and put\r","them away in his pocket; for although he could not see them he could\r","feel them, and when he had buttoned his coat he knew they were safe for\r","the present.\r","\r","The travellers now resumed their walk toward the cottage, which they\r","presently reached. It was a pretty place, with vines growing thickly\r","over the broad front porch. The door stood open and a table was set in\r","the front room, with four chairs drawn up to it. On the table were\r","plates, knives and forks, and dishes of bread, meat and fruits. The meat\r","was smoking hot and the knives and forks were performing strange antics\r","and jumping here and there in quite a puzzling way. But not a single\r","person appeared to be in the room.\r","\r","\"How funny!\" exclaimed Dorothy, who with Zeb and the Wizard now stood in\r","the doorway.\r","\r","A peal of merry laughter answered her, and the knives and forks fell to\r","the plates with a clatter. One of the chairs pushed back from the table,\r","and this was so astonishing and mysterious that Dorothy was almost\r","tempted to run away in fright.\r","\r","\"Here are strangers, mama!\" cried the shrill and childish voice of some\r","unseen person.\r","\r","\"So I see, my dear,\" answered another voice, soft and womanly.\r","\r","\"What do you want?\" demanded a third voice, in a stern, gruff accent.\r","\r","\"Well, well!\" said the Wizard; \"are there really people in this room?\"\r","\r","\"Of course,\" replied the man's voice.\r","\r","\"And--pardon me for the foolish question--but, are you all invisible?\"\r","\r","\"Surely,\" the woman answered, repeating her low, rippling laughter.\r","\"Are you surprised that you are unable to see the people of Voe?\"\r","\r","\"Why, yes,\" stammered the Wizard. \"All the people I have ever met before\r","were very plain to see.\"\r","\r","\"Where do you come from, then?\" asked the woman, in a curious tone.\r","\r","\"We belong upon the face of the earth,\" explained the Wizard, \"but\r","recently, during an earthquake, we fell down a crack and landed in the\r","Country of the Mangaboos.\"\r","\r","\"Dreadful creatures!\" exclaimed the woman's voice. \"I've heard of them.\"\r","\r","\"They walled us up in a mountain,\" continued the Wizard; \"but we found\r","there was a tunnel through to this side, so we came here. It is a\r","beautiful place. What do you call it?\"\r","\r","\"It is the Valley of Voe.\"\r","\r","\"Thank you. We have seen no people since we arrived, so we came to this\r","house to enquire our way.\"\r","\r","\"Are you hungry?\" asked the woman's voice.\r","\r","\"I could eat something,\" said Dorothy.\r","\r","\"So could I,\" added Zeb.\r","\r","\"But we do not wish to intrude, I assure you,\" the Wizard hastened to\r","say.\r","\r","\"That's all right,\" returned the man's voice, more pleasantly than\r","before. \"You are welcome to what we have.\"\r","\r","As he spoke the voice came so near to Zeb that he jumped back in alarm.\r","Two childish voices laughed merrily at this action, and Dorothy was sure\r","they were in no danger among such light-hearted folks, even if those\r","folks couldn't be seen.\r","\r","\"What curious animal is that which is eating the grass on my lawn?\"\r","enquired the man's voice.\r","\r","\"That's Jim,\" said the girl. \"He's a horse.\"\r","\r","\"What is he good for?\" was the next question.\r","\r","\"He draws the buggy you see fastened to him, and we ride in the buggy\r","instead of walking,\" she explained.\r","\r","\"Can he fight?\" asked the man's voice.\r","\r","\"No! he can kick pretty hard with his heels, and bite a little; but Jim\r","can't 'zactly fight,\" she replied.\r","\r","\"Then the bears will get him,\" said one of the children's voices.\r","\r","\"Bears!\" exclaimed Dorothy. \"Are these bears here?\"\r","\r","\"That is the one evil of our country,\" answered the invisible man. \"Many\r","large and fierce bears roam in the Valley of Voe, and when they can\r","catch any of us they eat us up; but as they cannot see us, we seldom get\r","caught.\"\r","\r","\"Are the bears invis'ble, too?\" asked the girl.\r","\r","\"Yes; for they eat of the dama-fruit, as we all do, and that keeps them\r","from being seen by any eye, whether human or animal.\"\r","\r","\"Does the dama-fruit grow on a low bush, and look something like a\r","peach?\" asked the Wizard.\r","\r","\"Yes,\" was the reply.\r","\r","\"If it makes you invis'ble, why do you eat it?\" Dorothy enquired.\r","\r","\"For two reasons, my dear,\" the woman's voice answered. \"The dama-fruit\r","is the most delicious thing that grows, and when it makes us invisible\r","the bears cannot find us to eat us up. But now, good wanderers, your\r","luncheon is on the table, so please sit down and eat as much as you\r","like.\"\r","\r","[Illustration]\r","\r","\r","\r","\r","CHAPTER 9.\r","\r","THEY FIGHT THE INVISIBLE BEARS\r","\r","\r","The strangers took their seats at the table willingly enough, for they\r","were all hungry and the platters were now heaped with good things to\r","eat. In front of each place was a plate bearing one of the delicious\r","dama-fruit, and the perfume that rose from these was so enticing and\r","sweet that they were sorely tempted to eat of them and become invisible.\r","\r","But Dorothy satisfied her hunger with other things, and her companions\r","did likewise, resisting the temptation.\r","\r","\"Why do you not eat the damas?\" asked the woman's voice.\r","\r","\"We don't want to get invis'ble,\" answered the girl.\r","\r","\"But if you remain visible the bears will see you and devour you,\" said\r","a girlish young voice, that belonged to one of the children. \"We who\r","live here much prefer to be invisible; for we can still hug and kiss one\r","another, and are quite safe from the bears.\"\r","\r","\"And we do not have to be so particular about our dress,\" remarked the\r","man.\r","\r","\"And mama can't tell whether my face is dirty or not!\" added the other\r","childish voice, gleefully.\r","\r","\"But I make you wash it, every time I think of it,\" said the mother;\r","\"for it stands to reason your face is dirty, Ianu, whether I can see it\r","or not.\"\r","\r","Dorothy laughed and stretched out her hands.\r","\r","\"Come here, please--Ianu and your sister--and let me feel of you,\" she\r","requested.\r","\r","They came to her willingly, and Dorothy passed her hands over their\r","faces and forms and decided one was a girl of about her own age and the\r","other a boy somewhat smaller. The girl's hair was soft and fluffy and\r","her skin as smooth as satin. When Dorothy gently touched her nose and\r","ears and lips they seemed to be well and delicately formed.\r","\r","\"If I could see you I am sure you would be beautiful,\" she declared.\r","\r","The girl laughed, and her mother said:\r","\r","\"We are not vain in the Valley of Voe, because we can not display our\r","beauty, and good actions and pleasant ways are what make us lovely to\r","our companions. Yet we can see and appreciate the beauties of nature,\r","the dainty flowers and trees, the green fields and the clear blue of the\r","sky.\"\r","\r","\"How about the birds and beasts and fishes?\" asked Zeb.\r","\r","\"The birds we cannot see, because they love to eat of the damas as much\r","as we do; yet we hear their sweet songs and enjoy them. Neither can we\r","see the cruel bears, for they also eat the fruit. But the fishes that\r","swim in our brooks we can see, and often we catch them to eat.\"\r","\r","\"It occurs to me you have a great deal to make you happy, even while\r","invisible,\" remarked the Wizard. \"Nevertheless, we prefer to remain\r","visible while we are in your valley.\"\r","\r","Just then Eureka came in, for she had been until now wandering outside\r","with Jim; and when the kitten saw the table set with food she cried out:\r","\r","\"Now you must feed me, Dorothy, for I'm half starved.\"\r","\r","The children were inclined to be frightened by the sight of the small\r","animal, which reminded them of the bears; but Dorothy reassured them by\r","explaining that Eureka was a pet and could do no harm even if she wished\r","to. Then, as the others had by this time moved away from the table, the\r","kitten sprang upon the chair and put her paws upon the cloth to see what\r","there was to eat. To her surprise an unseen hand clutched her and held\r","her suspended in the air. Eureka was frantic with terror, and tried to\r","scratch and bite, so the next moment she was dropped to the floor.\r","\r","\"Did you see that, Dorothy?\" she gasped.\r","\r","\"Yes, dear,\" her mistress replied; \"there are people living in this\r","house, although we cannot see them. And you must have better manners,\r","Eureka, or something worse will happen to you.\"\r","\r","She placed a plate of food upon the floor and the kitten ate greedily.\r","\r","\"Give me that nice-smelling fruit I saw on the table,\" she begged, when\r","she had cleaned the plate.\r","\r","\"Those are damas,\" said Dorothy, \"and you must never even taste them,\r","Eureka, or you'll get invis'ble, and then we can't see you at all.\"\r","\r","The kitten gazed wistfully at the forbidden fruit.\r","\r","\"Does it hurt to be invis'ble?\" she asked.\r","\r","\"I don't know,\" Dorothy answered; \"but it would hurt me dre'fully to\r","lose you.\"\r","\r","\"Very well, I won't touch it,\" decided the kitten; \"but you must keep it\r","away from me, for the smell is very tempting.\"\r","\r","\"Can you tell us, sir or ma'am,\" said the Wizard, addressing the air\r","because he did not quite know where the unseen people stood, \"if there\r","is any way we can get out of your beautiful Valley, and on top of the\r","Earth again.\"\r","\r","\"Oh, one can leave the Valley easily enough,\" answered the man's voice;\r","\"but to do so you must enter a far less pleasant country. As for\r","reaching the top of the earth, I have never heard that it is possible to\r","do that, and if you succeeded in getting there you would probably fall\r","off.\"\r","\r","\"Oh, no,\" said Dorothy, \"we've been there, and we know.\"\r","\r","\"The Valley of Voe is certainly a charming place,\" resumed the Wizard;\r","\"but we cannot be contented in any other land than our own, for long.\r","Even if we should come to unpleasant places on our way it is necessary,\r","in order to reach the earth's surface, to keep moving on toward it.\"\r","\r","\"In that case,\" said the man, \"it will be best for you to cross our\r","Valley and mount the spiral staircase inside the Pyramid Mountain. The\r","top of that mountain is lost in the clouds, and when you reach it you\r","will be in the awful Land of Naught, where the Gargoyles live.\"\r","\r","\"What are Gargoyles?\" asked Zeb.\r","\r","\"I do not know, young sir. Our greatest Champion, Overman-Anu, once\r","climbed the spiral stairway and fought nine days with the Gargoyles\r","before he could escape them and come back; but he could never be induced\r","to describe the dreadful creatures, and soon afterward a bear caught\r","him and ate him up.\"\r","\r","The wanderers were rather discouraged by this gloomy report, but Dorothy\r","said with a sigh:\r","\r","\"If the only way to get home is to meet the Gurgles, then we've got to\r","meet 'em. They can't be worse than the Wicked Witch or the Nome King.\"\r","\r","\"But you must remember you had the Scarecrow and the Tin Woodman to help\r","you conquer those enemies,\" suggested the Wizard. \"Just now, my dear,\r","there is not a single warrior in your company.\"\r","\r","\"Oh, I guess Zeb could fight if he had to. Couldn't you, Zeb?\" asked the\r","little girl.\r","\r","\"Perhaps; if I had to,\" answered Zeb, doubtfully.\r","\r","\"And you have the jointed sword that you chopped the veg'table Sorcerer\r","in two with,\" the girl said to the little man.\r","\r","\"True,\" he replied; \"and in my satchel are other useful things to fight\r","with.\"\r","\r","\"What the Gargoyles most dread is a noise,\" said the man's voice. \"Our\r","Champion told me that when he shouted his battle-cry the creatures\r","shuddered and drew back, hesitating to continue the combat. But they\r","were in great numbers, and the Champion could not shout much because he\r","had to save his breath for fighting.\"\r","\r","\"Very good,\" said the Wizard; \"we can all yell better than we can fight,\r","so we ought to defeat the Gargoyles.\"\r","\r","\"But tell me,\" said Dorothy, \"how did such a brave Champion happen to\r","let the bears eat him? And if he was invis'ble, and the bears invis'ble,\r","who knows that they really ate him up?\"\r","\r","\"The Champion had killed eleven bears in his time,\" returned the unseen\r","man; \"and we know this is true because when any creature is dead the\r","invisible charm of the dama-fruit ceases to be active, and the slain one\r","can be plainly seen by all eyes. When the Champion killed a bear\r","everyone could see it; and when the bears killed the Champion we all saw\r","several pieces of him scattered about, which of course disappeared again\r","when the bears devoured them.\"\r","\r","They now bade farewell to the kind but unseen people of the cottage, and\r","after the man had called their attention to a high, pyramid-shaped\r","mountain on the opposite side of the Valley, and told them how to travel\r","in order to reach it, they again started upon their journey.\r","\r","They followed the course of a broad stream and passed several more\r","pretty cottages; but of course they saw no one, nor did any one speak to\r","them. Fruits and flowers grew plentifully all about, and there were many\r","of the delicious damas that the people of Voe were so fond of.\r","\r","About noon they stopped to allow Jim to rest in the shade of a pretty\r","orchard, and while they plucked and ate some of the cherries and plums\r","that grew there a soft voice suddenly said to them:\r","\r","\"There are bears near by. Be careful.\"\r","\r","The Wizard got out his sword at once, and Zeb grabbed the horse-whip.\r","Dorothy climbed into the buggy, although Jim had been unharnessed from\r","it and was grazing some distance away.\r","\r","The owner of the unseen voice laughed lightly and said:\r","\r","\"You cannot escape the bears that way.\"\r","\r","\"How _can_ we 'scape?\" asked Dorothy, nervously, for an unseen danger is\r","always the hardest to face.\r","\r","\"You must take to the river,\" was the reply. \"The bears will not venture\r","upon the water.\"\r","\r","\"But we would be drowned!\" exclaimed the girl.\r","\r","\"Oh, there is no need of that,\" said the voice, which from its gentle\r","tones seemed to belong to a young girl. \"You are strangers in the Valley\r","of Voe, and do not seem to know our ways; so I will try to save you.\"\r","\r","The next moment a broad-leaved plant was jerked from the ground where it\r","grew and held suspended in the air before the Wizard.\r","\r","[Illustration: ESCAPING THE INVISIBLE BEARS.]\r","\r","\"Sir,\" said the voice, \"you must rub these leaves upon the soles of\r","all your feet, and then you will be able to walk upon the water without\r","sinking below the surface. It is a secret the bears do not know, and we\r","people of Voe usually walk upon the water when we travel, and so escape\r","our enemies.\"\r","\r","\"Thank you!\" cried the Wizard, joyfully, and at once rubbed a leaf upon\r","the soles of Dorothy's shoes and then upon his own. The girl took a leaf\r","and rubbed it upon the kitten's paws, and the rest of the plant was\r","handed to Zeb, who, after applying it to his own feet, carefully rubbed\r","it upon all four of Jim's hoofs and then upon the tires of the\r","buggy-wheels. He had nearly finished this last task when a low growling\r","was suddenly heard and the horse began to jump around and kick viciously\r","with his heels.\r","\r","\"Quick! To the water, or you are lost!\" cried their unseen friend, and\r","without hesitation the Wizard drew the buggy down the bank and out upon\r","the broad river, for Dorothy was still seated in it with Eureka in her\r","arms. They did not sink at all, owing to the virtues of the strange\r","plant they had used, and when the buggy was in the middle of the stream\r","the Wizard returned to the bank to assist Zeb and Jim.\r","\r","The horse was plunging madly about, and two or three deep gashes\r","appeared upon its flanks, from which the blood flowed freely.\r","\r","\"Run for the river!\" shouted the Wizard, and Jim quickly freed himself\r","from his unseen tormenters by a few vicious kicks and then obeyed. As\r","soon as he trotted out upon the surface of the river he found himself\r","safe from pursuit, and Zeb was already running across the water toward\r","Dorothy.\r","\r","As the little Wizard turned to follow them he felt a hot breath against\r","his cheek and heard a low, fierce growl. At once he began stabbing at\r","the air with his sword, and he knew that he had struck some substance\r","because when he drew back the blade it was dripping with blood. The\r","third time that he thrust out the weapon there was a loud roar and a\r","fall, and suddenly at his feet appeared the form of a great red bear,\r","which was nearly as big as the horse and much stronger and fiercer. The\r","beast was quite dead from the sword thrusts, and after a glance at its\r","terrible claws and sharp teeth the little man turned in a panic and\r","rushed out upon the water, for other menacing growls told him more bears\r","were near.\r","\r","On the river, however, the adventurers seemed to be perfectly safe.\r","Dorothy and the buggy had floated slowly down stream with the current of\r","the water, and the others made haste to join her. The Wizard opened his\r","satchel and got out some sticking-plaster with which he mended the cuts\r","Jim had received from the claws of the bears.\r","\r","\"I think we'd better stick to the river, after this,\" said Dorothy. \"If\r","our unknown friend hadn't warned us, and told us what to do, we would\r","all be dead by this time.\"\r","\r","\"That is true,\" agreed the Wizard, \"and as the river seems to be flowing\r","in the direction of the Pyramid Mountain it will be the easiest way for\r","us to travel.\"\r","\r","Zeb hitched Jim to the buggy again, and the horse trotted along and drew\r","them rapidly over the smooth water. The kitten was at first dreadfully\r","afraid of getting wet, but Dorothy let her down and soon Eureka was\r","frisking along beside the buggy without being scared a bit. Once a\r","little fish swam too near the surface, and the kitten grabbed it in her\r","mouth and ate it up as quick as a wink; but Dorothy cautioned her to be\r","careful what she ate in this valley of enchantments, and no more fishes\r","were careless enough to swim within reach.\r","\r","After a journey of several hours they came to a point where the river\r","curved, and they found they must cross a mile or so of the Valley before\r","they came to the Pyramid Mountain. There were few houses in this part,\r","and few orchards or flowers; so our friends feared they might encounter\r","more of the savage bears, which they had learned to dread with all their\r","hearts.\r","\r","\"You'll have to make a dash, Jim,\" said the Wizard, \"and run as fast as\r","you can go.\"\r","\r","\"All right,\" answered the horse; \"I'll do my best. But you must remember\r","I'm old, and my dashing days are past and gone.\"\r","\r","All three got into the buggy and Zeb picked up the reins, though Jim\r","needed no guidance of any sort. The horse was still smarting from the\r","sharp claws of the invisible bears, and as soon as he was on land and\r","headed toward the mountain the thought that more of those fearsome\r","creatures might be near acted as a spur and sent him galloping along in\r","a way that made Dorothy catch her breath.\r","\r","Then Zeb, in a spirit of mischief, uttered a growl like that of the\r","bears, and Jim pricked up his ears and fairly flew. His boney legs moved\r","so fast they could scarcely be seen, and the Wizard clung fast to the\r","seat and yelled \"Whoa!\" at the top of his voice.\r","\r","\"I--I'm 'fraid he's--he's running away!\" gasped Dorothy.\r","\r","\"I _know_ he is,\" said Zeb; \"but no bear can catch him if he keeps up\r","that gait--and the harness or the buggy don't break.\"\r","\r","Jim did not make a mile a minute; but almost before they were aware of\r","it he drew up at the foot of the mountain, so suddenly that the Wizard\r","and Zeb both sailed over the dashboard and landed in the soft\r","grass--where they rolled over several times before they stopped.\r","Dorothy nearly went with them, but she was holding fast to the iron rail\r","of the seat, and that saved her. She squeezed the kitten, though, until\r","it screeched; and then the old cab-horse made several curious sounds\r","that led the little girl to suspect he was laughing at them all.\r","\r","[Illustration]\r","\r","\r","\r","\r","CHAPTER 10.\r","\r","THE BRAIDED MAN OF PYRAMID MOUNTAIN\r","\r","\r","The mountain before them was shaped like a cone and was so tall that its\r","point was lost in the clouds. Directly facing the place where Jim had\r","stopped was an arched opening leading to a broad stairway. The stairs\r","were cut in the rock inside the mountain, and they were broad and not\r","very steep, because they circled around like a cork-screw, and at the\r","arched opening where the flight began the circle was quite big. At the\r","foot of the stairs was a sign reading:\r","\r","        WARNING.\r","  These steps lead to the\r","        Land of the Gargoyles.\r","    DANGER! KEEP OUT.\r","\r","\"I wonder how Jim is ever going to draw the buggy up so many stairs,\"\r","said Dorothy, gravely.\r","\r","\"No trouble at all,\" declared the horse, with a contemptuous neigh.\r","\"Still, I don't care to drag any passengers. You'll all have to walk.\"\r","\r","\"Suppose the stairs get steeper?\" suggested Zeb, doubtfully.\r","\r","\"Then you'll have to boost the buggy-wheels, that's all,\" answered Jim.\r","\r","\"We'll try it, anyway,\" said the Wizard. \"It's the only way to get out\r","of the Valley of Voe.\"\r","\r","So they began to ascend the stairs, Dorothy and the Wizard first, Jim\r","next, drawing the buggy, and then Zeb to watch that nothing happened to\r","the harness.\r","\r","The light was dim, and soon they mounted into total darkness, so that\r","the Wizard was obliged to get out his lanterns to light the way. But\r","this enabled them to proceed steadily until they came to a landing where\r","there was a rift in the side of the mountain that let in both light and\r","air. Looking through this opening they could see the Valley of Voe lying\r","far below them, the cottages seeming like toy houses from that distance.\r","\r","After resting a few moments they resumed their climb, and still the\r","stairs were broad and low enough for Jim to draw the buggy easily after\r","him. The old horse panted a little, and had to stop often to get his\r","breath. At such times they were all glad to wait for him, for\r","continually climbing up stairs is sure to make one's legs ache.\r","\r","They wound about, always going upward, for some time. The lights from\r","the lanterns dimly showed the way, but it was a gloomy journey, and they\r","were pleased when a broad streak of light ahead assured them they were\r","coming to a second landing.\r","\r","Here one side of the mountain had a great hole in it, like the mouth of\r","a cavern, and the stairs stopped at the near edge of the floor and\r","commenced ascending again at the opposite edge.\r","\r","The opening in the mountain was on the side opposite to the Valley of\r","Voe, and our travellers looked out upon a strange scene. Below them was\r","a vast space, at the bottom of which was a black sea with rolling\r","billows, through which little tongues of flame constantly shot up. Just\r","above them, and almost on a level with their platform, were banks of\r","rolling clouds which constantly shifted position and changed color. The\r","blues and greys were very beautiful, and Dorothy noticed that on the\r","cloud banks sat or reclined fleecy, shadowy forms of beautiful beings\r","who must have been the Cloud Fairies. Mortals who stand upon the earth\r","and look up at the sky cannot often distinguish these forms, but our\r","friends were now so near to the clouds that they observed the dainty\r","fairies very clearly.\r","\r","\"Are they real?\" asked Zeb, in an awed voice.\r","\r","\"Of course,\" replied Dorothy, softly. \"They are the Cloud Fairies.\"\r","\r","\"They seem like open-work,\" remarked the boy, gazing intently. \"If I\r","should squeeze one, there wouldn't be anything left of it.\"\r","\r","In the open space between the clouds and the black, bubbling sea far\r","beneath, could be seen an occasional strange bird winging its way\r","swiftly through the air. These birds were of enormous size, and reminded\r","Zeb of the rocs he had read about in the Arabian Nights. They had fierce\r","eyes and sharp talons and beaks, and the children hoped none of them\r","would venture into the cavern.\r","\r","\"Well, I declare!\" suddenly exclaimed the little Wizard. \"What in the\r","world is this?\"\r","\r","They turned around and found a man standing on the floor in the center\r","of the cave, who bowed very politely when he saw he had attracted their\r","attention. He was a very old man, bent nearly double; but the queerest\r","thing about him was his white hair and beard. These were so long that\r","they reached to his feet, and both the hair and the beard were\r","carefully plaited into many braids, and the end of each braid fastened\r","with a bow of colored ribbon.\r","\r","\"Where did you come from?\" asked Dorothy, wonderingly.\r","\r","\"No place at all,\" answered the man with the braids; \"that is, not\r","recently. Once I lived on top the earth, but for many years I have had\r","my factory in this spot--half way up Pyramid Mountain.\"\r","\r","\"Are we only half way up?\" enquired the boy, in a discouraged tone.\r","\r","\"I believe so, my lad,\" replied the braided man. \"But as I have never\r","been in either direction, down or up, since I arrived, I cannot be\r","positive whether it is exactly half way or not.\"\r","\r","\"Have you a factory in this place?\" asked the Wizard, who had been\r","examining the strange personage carefully.\r","\r","\"To be sure,\" said the other. \"I am a great inventor, you must know, and\r","I manufacture my products in this lonely spot.\"\r","\r","\"What are your products?\" enquired the Wizard.\r","\r","\"Well, I make Assorted Flutters for flags and bunting, and a superior\r","grade of Rustles for ladies' silk gowns.\"\r","\r","\"I thought so,\" said the Wizard, with a sigh. \"May we examine some of\r","these articles?\"\r","\r","[Illustration: THE CLOUD FAIRIES.]\r","\r","[Illustration: THE BRAIDED MAN.]\r","\r","\"Yes, indeed; come into my shop, please,\" and the braided man turned and\r","led the way into a smaller cave, where he evidently lived. Here, on a\r","broad shelf, were several card-board boxes of various sizes, each tied\r","with cotton cord.\r","\r","\"This,\" said the man, taking up a box and handling it gently, \"contains\r","twelve dozen rustles--enough to last any lady a year. Will you buy it,\r","my dear?\" he asked, addressing Dorothy.\r","\r","\"My gown isn't silk,\" she said, smiling.\r","\r","\"Never mind. When you open the box the rustles will escape, whether you\r","are wearing a silk dress or not,\" said the man, seriously. Then he\r","picked up another box. \"In this,\" he continued, \"are many assorted\r","flutters. They are invaluable to make flags flutter on a still day, when\r","there is no wind. You, sir,\" turning to the Wizard, \"ought to have this\r","assortment. Once you have tried my goods I am sure you will never be\r","without them.\"\r","\r","\"I have no money with me,\" said the Wizard, evasively.\r","\r","\"I do not want money,\" returned the braided man, \"for I could not spend\r","it in this deserted place if I had it. But I would like very much a blue\r","hair-ribbon. You will notice my braids are tied with yellow, pink,\r","brown, red, green, white and black; but I have no blue ribbons.\"\r","\r","\"I'll get you one!\" cried Dorothy, who was sorry for the poor man; so\r","she ran back to the buggy and took from her suit-case a pretty blue\r","ribbon. It did her good to see how the braided man's eyes sparkled when\r","he received this treasure.\r","\r","\"You have made me very, very happy, my dear!\" he exclaimed; and then he\r","insisted on the Wizard taking the box of flutters and the little girl\r","accepting the box of rustles.\r","\r","\"You may need them, some time,\" he said, \"and there is really no use in\r","my manufacturing these things unless somebody uses them.\"\r","\r","\"Why did you leave the surface of the earth?\" enquired the Wizard.\r","\r","\"I could not help it. It is a sad story, but if you will try to restrain\r","your tears I will tell you about it. On earth I was a manufacturer of\r","Imported Holes for American Swiss Cheese, and I will acknowledge that I\r","supplied a superior article, which was in great demand. Also I made\r","pores for porous plasters and high-grade holes for doughnuts and\r","buttons. Finally I invented a new Adjustable Post-hole, which I thought\r","would make my fortune. I manufactured a large quantity of these\r","post-holes, and having no room in which to store them I set them all end\r","to end and put the top one in the ground. That made an extraordinary\r","long hole, as you may imagine, and reached far down into the earth; and,\r","as I leaned over it to try to see to the bottom, I lost my balance and\r","tumbled in. Unfortunately, the hole led directly into the vast space you\r","see outside this mountain; but I managed to catch a point of rock that\r","projected from this cavern, and so saved myself from tumbling headlong\r","into the black waves beneath, where the tongues of flame that dart out\r","would certainly have consumed me. Here, then, I made my home; and\r","although it is a lonely place I amuse myself making rustles and\r","flutters, and so get along very nicely.\"\r","\r","When the braided man had completed this strange tale Dorothy nearly\r","laughed, because it was all so absurd; but the Wizard tapped his\r","forehead significantly, to indicate that he thought the poor man was\r","crazy. So they politely bade him good day, and went back to the outer\r","cavern to resume their journey.\r","\r","[Illustration]\r","\r","\r","\r","\r","CHAPTER 11.\r","\r","THEY MEET THE WOODEN GARGOYLES\r","\r","\r","Another breathless climb brought our adventurers to a third landing\r","where there was a rift in the mountain. On peering out all they could\r","see was rolling banks of clouds, so thick that they obscured all else.\r","\r","But the travellers were obliged to rest, and while they were sitting on\r","the rocky floor the Wizard felt in his pocket and brought out the nine\r","tiny piglets. To his delight they were now plainly visible, which proved\r","that they had passed beyond the influence of the magical Valley of Voe.\r","\r","\"Why, we can see each other again!\" cried one, joyfully.\r","\r","\"Yes,\" sighed Eureka; \"and I also can see you again, and the sight\r","makes me dreadfully hungry. Please, Mr. Wizard, may I eat just one of\r","the fat little piglets? You'd never miss _one_ of them, I'm sure!\"\r","\r","\"What a horrid, savage beast!\" exclaimed a piglet; \"and after we've been\r","such good friends, too, and played with one another!\"\r","\r","\"When I'm not hungry, I love to play with you all,\" said the kitten,\r","demurely; \"but when my stomach is empty it seems that nothing would fill\r","it so nicely as a fat piglet.\"\r","\r","\"And we trusted you so!\" said another of the nine, reproachfully.\r","\r","\"And thought you were respectable!\" said another.\r","\r","\"It seems we were mistaken,\" declared a third, looking at the kitten\r","timorously, \"no one with such murderous desires should belong to our\r","party, I'm sure.\"\r","\r","\"You see, Eureka,\" remarked Dorothy, reprovingly, \"you are making\r","yourself disliked. There are certain things proper for a kitten to eat;\r","but I never heard of a kitten eating a pig, under _any_ cir'stances.\"\r","\r","\"Did you ever see such little pigs before?\" asked the kitten. \"They are\r","no bigger than mice, and I'm sure mice are proper for me to eat.\"\r","\r","\"It isn't the bigness, dear; its the variety,\" replied the girl. \"These\r","are Mr. Wizard's pets, just as you are my pet, and it wouldn't be any\r","more proper for you to eat them than it would be for Jim to eat you.\"\r","\r","\"And that's just what I shall do if you don't let those little balls of\r","pork alone,\" said Jim, glaring at the kitten with his round, big eyes.\r","\"If you injure any one of them I'll chew you up instantly.\"\r","\r","The kitten looked at the horse thoughtfully, as if trying to decide\r","whether he meant it or not.\r","\r","\"In that case,\" she said, \"I'll leave them alone. You haven't many teeth\r","left, Jim, but the few you have are sharp enough to make me shudder. So\r","the piglets will be perfectly safe, hereafter, as far as I am\r","concerned.\"\r","\r","\"That is right, Eureka,\" remarked the Wizard, earnestly. \"Let us all be\r","a happy family and love one another.\"\r","\r","Eureka yawned and stretched herself.\r","\r","\"I've always loved the piglets,\" she said; \"but they don't love me.\"\r","\r","\"No one can love a person he's afraid of,\" asserted Dorothy. \"If you\r","behave, and don't scare the little pigs, I'm sure they'll grow very fond\r","of you.\"\r","\r","The Wizard now put the nine tiny ones back into his pocket and the\r","journey was resumed.\r","\r","\"We must be pretty near the top, now,\" said the boy, as they climbed\r","wearily up the dark, winding stairway.\r","\r","\"The Country of the Gurgles can't be far from the top of the earth,\"\r","remarked Dorothy. \"It isn't very nice down here. I'd like to get home\r","again, I'm sure.\"\r","\r","No one replied to this, because they found they needed all their breath\r","for the climb. The stairs had become narrower and Zeb and the Wizard\r","often had to help Jim pull the buggy from one step to another, or keep\r","it from jamming against the rocky walls.\r","\r","At last, however, a dim light appeared ahead of them, which grew clearer\r","and stronger as they advanced.\r","\r","\"Thank goodness we're nearly there!\" panted the little Wizard.\r","\r","Jim, who was in advance, saw the last stair before him and stuck his\r","head above the rocky sides of the stairway. Then he halted, ducked down\r","and began to back up, so that he nearly fell with the buggy onto the\r","others.\r","\r","\"Let's go down again!\" he said, in his hoarse voice.\r","\r","\"Nonsense!\" snapped the tired Wizard. \"What's the matter with you, old\r","man?\"\r","\r","\"Everything,\" grumbled the horse. \"I've taken a look at this place, and\r","it's no fit country for real creatures to go to. Everything's dead, up\r","there--no flesh or blood or growing thing anywhere.\"\r","\r","\"Never mind; we can't turn back,\" said Dorothy; \"and we don't intend to\r","stay there, anyhow.\"\r","\r","\"It's dangerous,\" growled Jim, in a stubborn tone.\r","\r","\"See here, my good steed,\" broke in the Wizard, \"little Dorothy and I\r","have been in many queer countries in our travels, and always escaped\r","without harm. We've even been to the marvelous Land of Oz--haven't we,\r","Dorothy?--so we don't much care what the Country of the Gargoyles is\r","like. Go ahead, Jim, and whatever happens we'll make the best of it.\"\r","\r","\"All right,\" answered the horse; \"this is your excursion, and not mine;\r","so if you get into trouble don't blame me.\"\r","\r","With this speech he bent forward and dragged the buggy up the remaining\r","steps. The others followed and soon they were all standing upon a broad\r","platform and gazing at the most curious and startling sight their eyes\r","had ever beheld.\r","\r","\"The Country of the Gargoyles is all wooden!\" exclaimed Zeb; and so it\r","was. The ground was sawdust and the pebbles scattered around were hard\r","knots from trees, worn smooth in course of time. There were odd wooden\r","houses, with carved wooden flowers in the front yards. The tree-trunks\r","were of coarse wood, but the leaves of the trees were shavings. The\r","patches of grass were splinters of wood, and where neither grass nor\r","sawdust showed was a solid wooden flooring. Wooden birds fluttered\r","among the trees and wooden cows were browsing upon the wooden grass; but\r","the most amazing things of all were the wooden people--the creatures\r","known as Gargoyles.\r","\r","These were very numerous, for the palace was thickly inhabited, and a\r","large group of the queer people clustered near, gazing sharply upon the\r","strangers who had emerged from the long spiral stairway.\r","\r","The Gargoyles were very small of stature, being less than three feet in\r","height. Their bodies were round, their legs short and thick and their\r","arms extraordinarily long and stout. Their heads were too big for their\r","bodies and their faces were decidedly ugly to look upon. Some had long,\r","curved noses and chins, small eyes and wide, grinning mouths. Others had\r","flat noses, protruding eyes, and ears that were shaped like those of an\r","elephant. There were many types, indeed, scarcely two being alike; but\r","all were equally disagreeable in appearance. The tops of their heads had\r","no hair, but were carved into a variety of fantastic shapes, some having\r","a row of points or balls around the top, other designs resembling\r","flowers or vegetables, and still others having squares that looked like\r","waffles cut criss-cross on their heads. They all wore short wooden wings\r","which were fastened to their wooden bodies by means of wooden hinges\r","with wooden screws, and with these wings they flew swiftly and\r","noiselessly here and there, their legs being of little use to them.\r","\r","This noiseless motion was one of the most peculiar things about the\r","Gargoyles. They made no sounds at all, either in flying or trying to\r","speak, and they conversed mainly by means of quick signals made with\r","their wooden fingers or lips. Neither was there any sound to be heard\r","anywhere throughout the wooden country. The birds did not sing, nor did\r","the cows moo; yet there was more than ordinary activity everywhere.\r","\r","The group of these queer creatures which was discovered clustered near\r","the stairs at first remained staring and motionless, glaring with evil\r","eyes at the intruders who had so suddenly appeared in their land. In\r","turn the Wizard and the children, the horse and the kitten, examined the\r","Gargoyles with the same silent attention.\r","\r","\"There's going to be trouble, I'm sure,\" remarked the horse. \"Unhitch\r","those tugs, Zeb, and set me free from the buggy, so I can fight\r","comfortably.\"\r","\r","\"Jim's right,\" sighed the Wizard. \"There's going to be trouble, and my\r","sword isn't stout enough to cut up those wooden bodies--so I shall have\r","to get out my revolvers.\"\r","\r","He got his satchel from the buggy and, opening it, took out two deadly\r","looking revolvers that made the children shrink back in alarm just to\r","look at.\r","\r","\"What harm can the Gurgles do?\" asked Dorothy. \"They have no weapons to\r","hurt us with.\"\r","\r","\"Each of their arms is a wooden club,\" answered the little man, \"and I'm\r","sure the creatures mean mischief, by the looks of their eyes. Even these\r","revolvers can merely succeed in damaging a few of their wooden bodies,\r","and after that we will be at their mercy.\"\r","\r","\"But why fight at all, in that case?\" asked the girl.\r","\r","\"So I may die with a clear conscience,\" returned the Wizard, gravely.\r","\"It's every man's duty to do the best he knows how; and I'm going to do\r","it.\"\r","\r","\"Wish I had an axe,\" said Zeb, who by now had unhitched the horse.\r","\r","\"If we had known we were coming we might have brought along several\r","other useful things,\" responded the Wizard. \"But we dropped into this\r","adventure rather unexpectedly.\"\r","\r","The Gargoyles had backed away a distance when they heard the sound of\r","talking, for although our friends had spoken in low tones their words\r","seemed loud in the silence surrounding them. But as soon as the\r","conversation ceased the grinning, ugly creatures arose in a flock and\r","flew swiftly toward the strangers, their long arms stretched out before\r","them like the bowsprits of a fleet of sail-boats. The horse had\r","especially attracted their notice, because it was the biggest and\r","strangest creature they had ever seen; so it became the center of their\r","first attack.\r","\r","But Jim was ready for them, and when he saw them coming he turned his\r","heels toward them and began kicking out as hard as he could. Crack!\r","crash! bang! went his iron-shod hoofs against the wooden bodies of the\r","Gargoyles, and they were battered right and left with such force that\r","they scattered like straws in the wind. But the noise and clatter seemed\r","as dreadful to them as Jim's heels, for all who were able swiftly turned\r","and flew away to a great distance. The others picked themselves up from\r","the ground one by one and quickly rejoined their fellows, so for a\r","moment the horse thought he had won the fight with ease.\r","\r","But the Wizard was not so confident.\r","\r","\"Those wooden things are impossible to hurt,\" he said, \"and all the\r","damage Jim has done to them is to knock a few splinters from their noses\r","and ears. That cannot make them look any uglier, I'm sure, and it is my\r","opinion they will soon renew the attack.\"\r","\r","\"What made them fly away?\" asked Dorothy.\r","\r","\"The noise, of course. Don't you remember how the Champion escaped them\r","by shouting his battle-cry?\"\r","\r","\"Suppose we escape down the stairs, too,\" suggested the boy. \"We have\r","time, just now, and I'd rather face the invis'ble bears than those\r","wooden imps.\"\r","\r","\"No,\" returned Dorothy, stoutly, \"it won't do to go back, for then we\r","would never get home. Let's fight it out.\"\r","\r","\"That is what I advise,\" said the Wizard. \"They haven't defeated us yet,\r","and Jim is worth a whole army.\"\r","\r","But the Gargoyles were clever enough not to attack the horse the next\r","time. They advanced in a great swarm, having been joined by many more of\r","their kind, and they flew straight over Jim's head to where the others\r","were standing.\r","\r","The Wizard raised one of his revolvers and fired into the throng of his\r","enemies, and the shot resounded like a clap of thunder in that silent\r","place.\r","\r","Some of the wooden beings fell flat upon the ground, where they quivered\r","and trembled in every limb; but most of them managed to wheel and escape\r","again to a distance.\r","\r","Zeb ran and picked up one of the Gargoyles that lay nearest to him. The\r","top of its head was carved into a crown and the Wizard's bullet had\r","struck it exactly in the left eye, which was a hard wooden knot. Half of\r","the bullet stuck in the wood and half stuck out, so it had been the jar\r","and the sudden noise that had knocked the creature down, more than the\r","fact that it was really hurt. Before this crowned Gargoyle had recovered\r","himself Zeb had wound a strap several times around its body, confining\r","its wings and arms so that it could not move. Then, having tied the\r","wooden creature securely, the boy buckled the strap and tossed his\r","prisoner into the buggy. By that time the others had all retired.\r","\r","[Illustration]\r","\r","\r","\r","\r","CHAPTER 12.\r","\r","A WONDERFUL ESCAPE\r","\r","\r","For a while the enemy hesitated to renew the attack. Then a few of them\r","advanced until another shot from the Wizard's revolver made them\r","retreat.\r","\r","\"That's fine,\" said Zeb. \"We've got 'em on the run now, sure enough.\"\r","\r","\"But only for a time,\" replied the Wizard, shaking his head gloomily.\r","\"These revolvers are good for six shots each, but when those are gone we\r","shall be helpless.\"\r","\r","The Gargoyles seemed to realize this, for they sent a few of their band\r","time after time to attack the strangers and draw the fire from the\r","little man's revolvers. In this way none of them was shocked by the\r","dreadful report more than once, for the main band kept far away and\r","each time a new company was sent into the battle. When the Wizard had\r","fired all of his twelve bullets he had caused no damage to the enemy\r","except to stun a few by the noise, and so he was no nearer to victory\r","than in the beginning of the fray.\r","\r","[Illustration: THE WIZARD FIRED INTO THE THRONG.]\r","\r","\"What shall we do now?\" asked Dorothy, anxiously.\r","\r","\"Let's yell--all together,\" said Zeb.\r","\r","\"And fight at the same time,\" added the Wizard. \"We will get near Jim,\r","so that he can help us, and each one must take some weapon and do the\r","best he can. I'll use my sword, although it isn't much account in this\r","affair. Dorothy must take her parasol and open it suddenly when the\r","wooden folks attack her. I haven't anything for you, Zeb.\"\r","\r","\"I'll use the king,\" said the boy, and pulled his prisoner out of the\r","buggy. The bound Gargoyle's arms extended far out beyond its head, so by\r","grasping its wrists Zeb found the king made a very good club. The boy\r","was strong for one of his years, having always worked upon a farm; so he\r","was likely to prove more dangerous to the enemy than the Wizard.\r","\r","When the next company of Gargoyles advanced, our adventurers began\r","yelling as if they had gone mad. Even the kitten gave a dreadfully\r","shrill scream and at the same time Jim the cab-horse neighed loudly.\r","This daunted the enemy for a time, but the defenders were soon out of\r","breath. Perceiving this, as well as the fact that there were no more of\r","the awful \"bangs\" to come from the revolvers, the Gargoyles advanced in\r","a swarm as thick as bees, so that the air was filled with them.\r","\r","Dorothy squatted upon the ground and put up her parasol, which nearly\r","covered her and proved a great protection. The Wizard's sword-blade\r","snapped into a dozen pieces at the first blow he struck against the\r","wooden people. Zeb pounded away with the Gargoyle he was using as a club\r","until he had knocked down dozens of foes; but at the last they clustered\r","so thickly about him that he no longer had room in which to swing his\r","arms. The horse performed some wonderful kicking and even Eureka\r","assisted when she leaped bodily upon the Gargoyles and scratched and bit\r","at them like a wild-cat.\r","\r","But all this bravery amounted to nothing at all. The wooden things wound\r","their long arms around Zeb and the Wizard and held them fast. Dorothy\r","was captured in the same way, and numbers of the Gargoyles clung to\r","Jim's legs, so weighting him down that the poor beast was helpless.\r","Eureka made a desperate dash to escape and scampered along the ground\r","like a streak; but a grinning Gargoyle flew after her and grabbed her\r","before she had gone very far.\r","\r","All of them expected nothing less than instant death; but to their\r","surprise the wooden creatures flew into the air with them and bore them\r","far away, over miles and miles of wooden country, until they came to a\r","wooden city. The houses of this city had many corners, being square and\r","six-sided and eight-sided. They were tower-like in shape and the best of\r","them seemed old and weather-worn; yet all were strong and substantial.\r","\r","To one of these houses which had neither doors nor windows, but only one\r","broad opening far up underneath the roof, the prisoners were brought by\r","their captors. The Gargoyles roughly pushed them into the opening, where\r","there was a platform, and then flew away and left them. As they had no\r","wings the strangers could not fly away, and if they jumped down from\r","such a height they would surely be killed. The creatures had sense\r","enough to reason that way, and the only mistake they made was in\r","supposing the earth people were unable to overcome such ordinary\r","difficulties.\r","\r","Jim was brought with the others, although it took a good many Gargoyles\r","to carry the big beast through the air and land him on the high\r","platform, and the buggy was thrust in after him because it belonged to\r","the party and the wooden folks had no idea what it was used for or\r","whether it was alive or not. When Eureka's captor had thrown the kitten\r","after the others the last Gargoyle silently disappeared, leaving our\r","friends to breathe freely once more.\r","\r","\"What an awful fight!\" said Dorothy, catching her breath in little\r","gasps.\r","\r","\"Oh, I don't know,\" purred Eureka, smoothing her ruffled fur with her\r","paw; \"we didn't manage to hurt anybody, and nobody managed to hurt us.\"\r","\r","\"Thank goodness we are together again, even if we are prisoners,\" sighed\r","the little girl.\r","\r","\"I wonder why they didn't kill us on the spot,\" remarked Zeb, who had\r","lost his king in the struggle.\r","\r","\"They are probably keeping us for some ceremony,\" the Wizard answered,\r","reflectively; \"but there is no doubt they intend to kill us as dead as\r","possible in a short time.\"\r","\r","\"As dead as poss'ble would be pretty dead, wouldn't it?\" asked Dorothy.\r","\r","\"Yes, my dear. But we have no need to worry about that just now. Let us\r","examine our prison and see what it is like.\"\r","\r","The space underneath the roof, where they stood, permitted them to see\r","on all sides of the tall building, and they looked with much curiosity\r","at the city spread out beneath them. Everything visible was made of\r","wood, and the scene seemed stiff and extremely unnatural.\r","\r","From their platform a stair descended into the house, and the children\r","and the Wizard explored it after lighting a lantern to show them the\r","way. Several stories of empty rooms rewarded their search, but nothing\r","more; so after a time they came back to the platform again. Had there\r","been any doors or windows in the lower rooms, or had not the boards of\r","the house been so thick and stout, escape would have been easy; but to\r","remain down below was like being in a cellar or the hold of a ship, and\r","they did not like the darkness or the damp smell.\r","\r","In this country, as in all others they had visited underneath the\r","earth's surface, there was no night, a constant and strong light coming\r","from some unknown source. Looking out, they could see into some of the\r","houses near them, where there were open windows in abundance, and were\r","able to mark the forms of the wooden Gargoyles moving about in their\r","dwellings.\r","\r","\"This seems to be their time of rest,\" observed the Wizard. \"All people\r","need rest, even if they are made of wood, and as there is no night here\r","they select a certain time of the day in which to sleep or doze.\"\r","\r","\"I feel sleepy myself,\" remarked Zeb, yawning.\r","\r","\"Why, where's Eureka?\" cried Dorothy, suddenly.\r","\r","They all looked around, but the kitten was no place to be seen.\r","\r","\"She's gone out for a walk,\" said Jim, gruffly.\r","\r","\"Where? On the roof?\" asked the girl.\r","\r","\"No; she just dug her claws into the wood and climbed down the sides of\r","this house to the ground.\"\r","\r","\"She couldn't climb _down_, Jim,\" said Dorothy. \"To climb means to go\r","up.\"\r","\r","\"Who said so?\" demanded the horse.\r","\r","\"My school-teacher said so; and she knows a lot, Jim.\"\r","\r","\"To 'climb down' is sometimes used as a figure of speech,\" remarked the\r","Wizard.\r","\r","\"Well, this was a figure of a cat,\" said Jim, \"and she _went_ down,\r","anyhow, whether she climbed or crept.\"\r","\r","\"Dear me! how careless Eureka is,\" exclaimed the girl, much distressed.\r","\"The Gurgles will get her, sure!\"\r","\r","\"Ha, ha!\" chuckled the old cab-horse; \"they're not 'Gurgles,' little\r","maid; they're Gargoyles.\"\r","\r","\"Never mind; they'll get Eureka, whatever they're called.\"\r","\r","\"No they won't,\" said the voice of the kitten, and Eureka herself\r","crawled over the edge of the platform and sat down quietly upon the\r","floor.\r","\r","\"Wherever have you been, Eureka?\" asked Dorothy, sternly.\r","\r","\"Watching the wooden folks. They're too funny for anything, Dorothy.\r","Just now they are all going to bed, and--what do you think?--they unhook\r","the hinges of their wings and put them in a corner until they wake up\r","again.\"\r","\r","\"What, the hinges?\"\r","\r","\"No; the wings.\"\r","\r","\"That,\" said Zeb, \"explains why this house is used by them for a prison.\r","If any of the Gargoyles act badly, and have to be put in jail, they are\r","brought here and their wings unhooked and taken away from them until\r","they promise to be good.\"\r","\r","The Wizard had listened intently to what Eureka had said.\r","\r","\"I wish we had some of those loose wings,\" he said.\r","\r","\"Could we fly with them?\" asked Dorothy.\r","\r","\"I think so. If the Gargoyles can unhook the wings then the power to fly\r","lies in the wings themselves, and not in the wooden bodies of the people\r","who wear them. So, if we had the wings, we could probably fly as well as\r","they do--at least while we are in their country and under the spell of\r","its magic.\"\r","\r","\"But how would it help us to be able to fly?\" questioned the girl.\r","\r","\"Come here,\" said the little man, and took her to one of the corners of\r","the building. \"Do you see that big rock standing on the hillside\r","yonder?\" he continued, pointing with his finger.\r","\r","\"Yes; it's a good way off, but I can see it,\" she replied.\r","\r","\"Well, inside that rock, which reaches up into the clouds, is an archway\r","very much like the one we entered when we climbed the spiral stairway\r","from the Valley of Voe. I'll get my spy-glass, and then you can see it\r","more plainly.\"\r","\r","He fetched a small but powerful telescope, which had been in his\r","satchel, and by its aid the little girl clearly saw the opening.\r","\r","\"Where does it lead to?\" she asked.\r","\r","\"That I cannot tell,\" said the Wizard; \"but we cannot now be far below\r","the earth's surface, and that entrance may lead to another stairway that\r","will bring us on top of our world again, where we belong. So, if we had\r","the wings, and could escape the Gargoyles, we might fly to that rock and\r","be saved.\"\r","\r","\"I'll get you the wings,\" said Zeb, who had thoughtfully listened to all\r","this. \"That is, if the kitten will show me where they are.\"\r","\r","\"But how can you get down?\" enquired the girl, wonderingly.\r","\r","For answer Zeb began to unfasten Jim's harness, strap by strap, and\r","to buckle one piece to another until he had made a long leather strip\r","that would reach to the ground.\r","\r","[Illustration: THE FIGHT WITH THE GARGOYLES.]\r","\r","\"I can climb down that, all right,\" he said.\r","\r","\"No you can't,\" remarked Jim, with a twinkle in his round eyes. \"You may\r","_go_ down, but you can only _climb_ up.\"\r","\r","\"Well, I'll climb up when I get back, then,\" said the boy, with a laugh.\r","\"Now, Eureka, you'll have to show me the way to those wings.\"\r","\r","\"You must be very quiet,\" warned the kitten; \"for if you make the least\r","noise the Gargoyles will wake up. They can hear a pin drop.\"\r","\r","\"I'm not going to drop a pin,\" said Zeb.\r","\r","He had fastened one end of the strap to a wheel of the buggy, and now he\r","let the line dangle over the side of the house.\r","\r","\"Be careful,\" cautioned Dorothy, earnestly.\r","\r","\"I will,\" said the boy, and let himself slide over the edge.\r","\r","The girl and the Wizard leaned over and watched Zeb work his way\r","carefully downward, hand over hand, until he stood upon the ground\r","below. Eureka clung with her claws to the wooden side of the house and\r","let herself down easily. Then together they crept away to enter the low\r","doorway of a neighboring dwelling.\r","\r","The watchers waited in breathless suspense until the boy again appeared,\r","his arms now full of the wooden wings.\r","\r","When he came to where the strap was hanging he tied the wings all in a\r","bunch to the end of the line, and the Wizard drew them up. Then the line\r","was let down again for Zeb to climb up by. Eureka quickly followed him,\r","and soon they were all standing together upon the platform, with eight\r","of the much prized wooden wings beside them.\r","\r","The boy was no longer sleepy, but full of energy and excitement. He put\r","the harness together again and hitched Jim to the buggy. Then, with the\r","Wizard's help, he tried to fasten some of the wings to the old\r","cab-horse.\r","\r","This was no easy task, because half of each one of the hinges of the\r","wings was missing, it being still fastened to the body of the Gargoyle\r","who had used it. However, the Wizard went once more to his\r","satchel--which seemed to contain a surprising variety of odds and\r","ends--and brought out a spool of strong wire, by means of which they\r","managed to fasten four of the wings to Jim's harness, two near his head\r","and two near his tail. They were a bit wiggley, but secure enough if\r","only the harness held together.\r","\r","The other four wings were then fastened to the buggy, two on each side,\r","for the buggy must bear the weight of the children and the Wizard as it\r","flew through the air.\r","\r","[Illustration: JIM FLUTTERED AND FLOUNDERED THROUGH THE AIR.]\r","\r","These preparations had not consumed a great deal of time, but the\r","sleeping Gargoyles were beginning to wake up and move around, and soon\r","some of them would be hunting for their missing wings. So the prisoners\r","resolved to leave their prison at once.\r","\r","They mounted into the buggy, Dorothy holding Eureka safe in her lap. The\r","girl sat in the middle of the seat, with Zeb and the Wizard on each side\r","of her. When all was ready the boy shook the reins and said:\r","\r","\"Fly away, Jim!\"\r","\r","\"Which wings must I flop first?\" asked the cab-horse, undecidedly.\r","\r","\"Flop them all together,\" suggested the Wizard.\r","\r","\"Some of them are crooked,\" objected the horse.\r","\r","\"Never mind; we will steer with the wings on the buggy,\" said Zeb. \"Just\r","you light out and make for that rock, Jim; and don't waste any time\r","about it, either.\"\r","\r","So the horse gave a groan, flopped its four wings all together, and flew\r","away from the platform. Dorothy was a little anxious about the success\r","of their trip, for the way Jim arched his long neck and spread out his\r","bony legs as he fluttered and floundered through the air was enough to\r","make anybody nervous. He groaned, too, as if frightened, and the wings\r","creaked dreadfully because the Wizard had forgotten to oil them; but\r","they kept fairly good time with the wings of the buggy, so that they\r","made excellent progress from the start. The only thing that anyone could\r","complain of with justice was the fact that they wobbled first up and\r","then down, as if the road were rocky instead of being as smooth as the\r","air could make it.\r","\r","The main point, however, was that they flew, and flew swiftly, if a bit\r","unevenly, toward the rock for which they had headed.\r","\r","Some of the Gargoyles saw them, presently, and lost no time in\r","collecting a band to pursue the escaping prisoners; so that when Dorothy\r","happened to look back she saw them coming in a great cloud that almost\r","darkened the sky.\r","\r","[Illustration]\r","\r","\r","\r","\r","CHAPTER 13.\r","\r","THE DEN OF THE DRAGONETTES\r","\r","\r","Our friends had a good start and were able to maintain it, for with\r","their eight wings they could go just as fast as could the Gargoyles. All\r","the way to the great rock the wooden people followed them, and when Jim\r","finally alighted at the mouth of the cavern the pursuers were still some\r","distance away.\r","\r","\"But, I'm afraid they'll catch us yet,\" said Dorothy, greatly excited.\r","\r","\"No; we must stop them,\" declared the Wizard. \"Quick Zeb, help me pull\r","off these wooden wings!\"\r","\r","They tore off the wings, for which they had no further use, and the\r","Wizard piled them in a heap just outside the entrance to the cavern.\r","Then he poured over them all the kerosene oil that was left in his\r","oil-can, and lighting a match set fire to the pile.\r","\r","The flames leaped up at once and the bonfire began to smoke and roar and\r","crackle just as the great army of wooden Gargoyles arrived. The\r","creatures drew back at once, being filled with fear and horror; for such\r","a dreadful thing as a fire they had never before known in all the\r","history of their wooden land.\r","\r","Inside the archway were several doors, leading to different rooms built\r","into the mountain, and Zeb and the Wizard lifted these wooden doors from\r","their hinges and tossed them all on the flames.\r","\r","\"That will prove a barrier for some time to come,\" said the little man,\r","smiling pleasantly all over his wrinkled face at the success of their\r","stratagem. \"Perhaps the flames will set fire to all that miserable\r","wooden country, and if it does the loss will be very small and the\r","Gargoyles never will be missed.
