But come, my children; let us explore\r","the mountain and discover which way we must go in order to escape from\r","this cavern, which is getting to be almost as hot as a bake-oven.\"\r","\r","To their disappointment there was within this mountain no regular flight\r","of steps by means of which they could mount to the earth's surface. A\r","sort of inclined tunnel led upward for a way, and they found the floor\r","of it both rough and steep. Then a sudden turn brought them to a narrow\r","gallery where the buggy could not pass. This delayed and bothered them\r","for a while, because they did not wish to leave the buggy behind them.\r","It carried their baggage and was useful to ride in wherever there were\r","good roads, and since it had accompanied them so far in their travels\r","they felt it their duty to preserve it. So Zeb and the Wizard set to\r","work and took off the wheels and the top, and then they put the buggy\r","edgewise, so it would take up the smallest space. In this position they\r","managed, with the aid of the patient cab-horse, to drag the vehicle\r","through the narrow part of the passage. It was not a great distance,\r","fortunately, and when the path grew broader they put the buggy together\r","again and proceeded more comfortably. But the road was nothing more than\r","a series of rifts or cracks in the mountain, and it went zig-zag in\r","every direction, slanting first up and then down until they were puzzled\r","as to whether they were any nearer to the top of the earth than when\r","they had started, hours before.\r","\r","\"Anyhow,\" said Dorothy, \"we've 'scaped those awful Gurgles, and that's\r","_one_ comfort!\"\r","\r","[Illustration: \"WHY IT'S A DRAGON!\"]\r","\r","\"Probably the Gargoyles are still busy trying to put out the fire,\"\r","returned the Wizard. \"But even if they succeeded in doing that it\r","would be very difficult for them to fly amongst these rocks; so I am\r","sure we need fear them no longer.\"\r","\r","Once in a while they would come to a deep crack in the floor, which made\r","the way quite dangerous; but there was still enough oil in the lanterns\r","to give them light, and the cracks were not so wide but that they were\r","able to jump over them. Sometimes they had to climb over heaps of loose\r","rock, where Jim could scarcely drag the buggy. At such times Dorothy,\r","Zeb and the Wizard all pushed behind, and lifted the wheels over the\r","roughest places; so they managed, by dint of hard work, to keep going.\r","But the little party was both weary and discouraged when at last, on\r","turning a sharp corner, the wanderers found themselves in a vast cave\r","arching high over their heads and having a smooth, level floor.\r","\r","The cave was circular in shape, and all around its edge, near to the\r","ground, appeared groups of dull yellow lights, two of them being always\r","side by side. These were motionless at first, but soon began to flicker\r","more brightly and to sway slowly from side to side and then up and down.\r","\r","\"What sort of a place is this?\" asked the boy, trying to see more\r","clearly through the gloom.\r","\r","\"I cannot imagine, I'm sure,\" answered the Wizard, also peering about.\r","\r","\"Woogh!\" snarled Eureka, arching her back until her hair stood straight\r","on end; \"it's a den of alligators, or crocodiles, or some other dreadful\r","creatures! Don't you see their terrible eyes?\"\r","\r","\"Eureka sees better in the dark than we can,\" whispered Dorothy. \"Tell\r","us, dear, what do the creatures look like?\" she asked, addressing her\r","pet.\r","\r","\"I simply can't describe 'em,\" answered the kitten, shuddering. \"Their\r","eyes are like pie-plates and their mouths like coal-scuttles. But their\r","bodies don't seem very big.\"\r","\r","\"Where are they?\" enquired the girl.\r","\r","\"They are in little pockets all around the edge of this cavern. Oh,\r","Dorothy--you can't imagine what horrid things they are! They're uglier\r","than the Gargoyles.\"\r","\r","\"Tut-tut! be careful how you criticise your neighbors,\" spoke a rasping\r","voice near by. \"As a matter of fact you are rather ugly-looking\r","creatures yourselves, and I'm sure mother has often told us we were the\r","loveliest and prettiest things in all the world.\"\r","\r","Hearing these words our friends turned in the direction of the sound,\r","and the Wizard held his lanterns so that their light would flood one of\r","the little pockets in the rock.\r","\r","\"Why, it's a dragon!\" he exclaimed.\r","\r","\"No,\" answered the owner of the big yellow eyes which were blinking at\r","them so steadily; \"you are wrong about that. We hope to grow to be\r","dragons some day, but just now we're only dragonettes.\"\r","\r","\"What's that?\" asked Dorothy, gazing fearfully at the great scaley head,\r","the yawning mouth and the big eyes.\r","\r","\"Young dragons, of course; but we are not allowed to call ourselves real\r","dragons until we get our full growth,\" was the reply. \"The big dragons\r","are very proud, and don't think children amount to much; but mother says\r","that some day we will all be very powerful and important.\"\r","\r","\"Where is your mother?\" asked the Wizard, anxiously looking around.\r","\r","\"She has gone up to the top of the earth to hunt for our dinner. If she\r","has good luck she will bring us an elephant, or a brace of rhinoceri, or\r","perhaps a few dozen people to stay our hunger.\"\r","\r","\"Oh; are you hungry?\" enquired Dorothy, drawing back.\r","\r","\"Very,\" said the dragonette, snapping its jaws.\r","\r","\"And--and--do you eat people?\"\r","\r","\"To be sure, when we can get them. But they've been very scarce for a\r","few years and we usually have to be content with elephants or\r","buffaloes,\" answered the creature, in a regretful tone.\r","\r","\"How old are you?\" enquired Zeb, who stared at the yellow eyes as if\r","fascinated.\r","\r","\"Quite young, I grieve to say; and all of my brothers and sisters that\r","you see here are practically my own age. If I remember rightly, we were\r","sixty-six years old the day before yesterday.\"\r","\r","\"But that isn't young!\" cried Dorothy, in amazement.\r","\r","\"No?\" drawled the dragonette; \"it seems to me very babyish.\"\r","\r","\"How old is your mother?\" asked the girl.\r","\r","\"Mother's about two thousand years old; but she carelessly lost track of\r","her age a few centuries ago and skipped several hundreds. She's a little\r","fussy, you know, and afraid of growing old, being a widow and still in\r","her prime.\"\r","\r","\"I should think she would be,\" agreed Dorothy. Then, after a moment's\r","thought, she asked: \"Are we friends or enemies? I mean, will you be good\r","to us, or do you intend to eat us?\"\r","\r","\"As for that, we dragonettes would love to eat you, my child; but\r","unfortunately mother has tied all our tails around the rocks at the back\r","of our individual caves, so that we can not crawl out to get you. If you\r","choose to come nearer we will make a mouthful of you in a wink; but\r","unless you do you will remain quite safe.\"\r","\r","There was a regretful accent in the creature's voice, and at the words\r","all the other dragonettes sighed dismally.\r","\r","Dorothy felt relieved. Presently she asked:\r","\r","\"Why did your mother tie your tails?\"\r","\r","\"Oh, she is sometimes gone for several weeks on her hunting trips, and\r","if we were not tied we would crawl all over the mountain and fight with\r","each other and get into a lot of mischief. Mother usually knows what she\r","is about, but she made a mistake this time; for you are sure to escape\r","us unless you come too near, and you probably won't do that.\"\r","\r","\"No, indeed!\" said the little girl. \"We don't wish to be eaten by such\r","awful beasts.\"\r","\r","\"Permit me to say,\" returned the dragonette, \"that you are rather\r","impolite to call us names, knowing that we cannot resent your insults.\r","We consider ourselves very beautiful in appearance, for mother has told\r","us so, and she knows. And we are of an excellent family and have a\r","pedigree that I challenge any humans to equal, as it extends back about\r","twenty thousand years, to the time of the famous Green Dragon of\r","Atlantis, who lived in a time when humans had not yet been created. Can\r","you match that pedigree, little girl?\"\r","\r","\"Well,\" said Dorothy, \"I was born on a farm in Kansas, and I guess\r","that's being just as 'spectable and haughty as living in a cave with\r","your tail tied to a rock. If it isn't I'll have to stand it, that's\r","all.\"\r","\r","\"Tastes differ,\" murmured the dragonette, slowly drooping its scaley\r","eyelids over its yellow eyes, until they looked like half-moons.\r","\r","Being reassured by the fact that the creatures could not crawl out of\r","their rock-pockets, the children and the Wizard now took time to examine\r","them more closely. The heads of the dragonettes were as big as barrels\r","and covered with hard, greenish scales that glittered brightly under the\r","light of the lanterns. Their front legs, which grew just back of their\r","heads, were also strong and big; but their bodies were smaller around\r","than their heads, and dwindled away in a long line until their tails\r","were slim as a shoe-string. Dorothy thought, if it had taken them\r","sixty-six years to grow to this size, that it would be fully a hundred\r","years more before they could hope to call themselves dragons, and that\r","seemed like a good while to wait to grow up.\r","\r","\"It occurs to me,\" said the Wizard, \"that we ought to get out of this\r","place before the mother dragon comes back.\"\r","\r","\"Don't hurry,\" called one of the dragonettes; \"mother will be glad to\r","meet you, I'm sure.\"\r","\r","\"You may be right,\" replied the Wizard, \"but we're a little particular\r","about associating with strangers. Will you kindly tell us which way your\r","mother went to get on top the earth?\"\r","\r","\"That is not a fair question to ask us,\" declared another dragonette.\r","\"For, if we told you truly, you might escape us altogether; and if we\r","told you an untruth we would be naughty and deserve to be punished.\"\r","\r","\"Then,\" decided Dorothy, \"we must find our way out the best we can.\"\r","\r","They circled all around the cavern, keeping a good distance away from\r","the blinking yellow eyes of the dragonettes, and presently discovered\r","that there were two paths leading from the wall opposite to the place\r","where they had entered. They selected one of these at a venture and\r","hurried along it as fast as they could go, for they had no idea when the\r","mother dragon would be back and were very anxious not to make her\r","acquaintance.\r","\r","[Illustration]\r","\r","\r","\r","\r","Chapter 14.\r","\r","OZMA USES THE MAGIC BELT\r","\r","\r","For a considerable distance the way led straight upward in a gentle\r","incline, and the wanderers made such good progress that they grew\r","hopeful and eager, thinking they might see sunshine at any minute. But\r","at length they came unexpectedly upon a huge rock that shut off the\r","passage and blocked them from proceeding a single step farther.\r","\r","This rock was separate from the rest of the mountain and was in motion,\r","turning slowly around and around as if upon a pivot. When first they\r","came to it there was a solid wall before them; but presently it revolved\r","until there was exposed a wide, smooth path across it to the other side.\r","This appeared so unexpectedly that they were unprepared to take\r","advantage of it at first, and allowed the rocky wall to swing around\r","again before they had decided to pass over. But they knew now that there\r","was a means of escape and so waited patiently until the path appeared\r","for the second time.\r","\r","The children and the Wizard rushed across the moving rock and sprang\r","into the passage beyond, landing safely though a little out of breath.\r","Jim the cab-horse came last, and the rocky wall almost caught him; for\r","just as he leaped to the floor of the further passage the wall swung\r","across it and a loose stone that the buggy wheels knocked against fell\r","into the narrow crack where the rock turned, and became wedged there.\r","\r","They heard a crunching, grinding sound, a loud snap, and the turn-table\r","came to a stop with its broadest surface shutting off the path from\r","which they had come.\r","\r","\"Never mind,\" said Zeb, \"we don't want to get back, anyhow.\"\r","\r","\"I'm not so sure of that,\" returned Dorothy. \"The mother dragon may come\r","down and catch us here.\"\r","\r","\"It is possible,\" agreed the Wizard, \"if this proves to be the path she\r","usually takes. But I have been examining this tunnel, and I do not see\r","any signs of so large a beast having passed through it.\"\r","\r","\"Then we're all right,\" said the girl, \"for if the dragon went the other\r","way she can't poss'bly get to us now.\"\r","\r","\"Of course not, my dear. But there is another thing to consider. The\r","mother dragon probably knows the road to the earth's surface, and if she\r","went the other way then we have come the wrong way,\" said the Wizard,\r","thoughtfully.\r","\r","\"Dear me!\" cried Dorothy. \"That would be unlucky, wouldn't it?\"\r","\r","\"Very. Unless this passage also leads to the top of the earth,\" said\r","Zeb. \"For my part, if we manage to get out of here I'll be glad it isn't\r","the way the dragon goes.\"\r","\r","\"So will I,\" returned Dorothy. \"It's enough to have your pedigree flung\r","in your face by those saucy dragonettes. No one knows what the mother\r","might do.\"\r","\r","They now moved on again, creeping slowly up another steep incline. The\r","lanterns were beginning to grow dim, and the Wizard poured the remaining\r","oil from one into the other, so that the one light would last longer.\r","But their journey was almost over, for in a short time they reached a\r","small cave from which there was no further outlet.\r","\r","They did not realize their ill fortune at first, for their hearts were\r","gladdened by the sight of a ray of sunshine coming through a small crack\r","in the roof of the cave, far overhead. That meant that their world--the\r","real world--was not very far away, and that the succession of perilous\r","adventures they had encountered had at last brought them near the\r","earth's surface, which meant home to them. But when the adventurers\r","looked more carefully around them they discovered that they were in a\r","strong prison from which there was no hope of escape.\r","\r","\"But we're _almost_ on earth again,\" cried Dorothy, \"for there is the\r","sun--the most _beau'ful_ sun that shines!\" and she pointed eagerly at\r","the crack in the distant roof.\r","\r","\"Almost on earth isn't being there,\" said the kitten, in a discontented\r","tone. \"It wouldn't be possible for even me to get up to that crack--or\r","through it if I got there.\"\r","\r","\"It appears that the path ends here,\" announced the Wizard, gloomily.\r","\r","\"And there is no way to go back,\" added Zeb, with a low whistle of\r","perplexity.\r","\r","\"I was sure it would come to this, in the end,\" remarked the old\r","cab-horse. \"Folks don't fall into the middle of the earth and then get\r","back again to tell of their adventures--not in real life. And the whole\r","thing has been unnatural because that cat and I are both able to talk\r","your language, and to understand the words you say.\"\r","\r","\"And so can the nine tiny piglets,\" added Eureka. \"Don't forget them,\r","for I may have to eat them, after all.\"\r","\r","\"I've heard animals talk before,\" said Dorothy, \"and no harm came of\r","it.\"\r","\r","\"Were you ever before shut up in a cave, far under the earth, with no\r","way of getting out?\" enquired the horse, seriously.\r","\r","\"No,\" answered Dorothy. \"But don't you lose heart, Jim, for I'm sure\r","this isn't the end of our story, by any means.\"\r","\r","The reference to the piglets reminded the Wizard that his pets had not\r","enjoyed much exercise lately, and must be tired of their prison in his\r","pocket. So he sat down upon the floor of the cave, brought the piglets\r","out one by one, and allowed them to run around as much as they pleased.\r","\r","\"My dears,\" he said to them, \"I'm afraid I've got you into a lot of\r","trouble, and that you will never again be able to leave this gloomy\r","cave.\"\r","\r","\"What's wrong?\" asked a piglet. \"We've been in the dark quite a while,\r","and you may as well explain what has happened.\"\r","\r","The Wizard told them of the misfortune that had overtaken the wanderers.\r","\r","\"Well,\" said another piglet, \"you are a wizard, are you not?\"\r","\r","\"I am,\" replied the little man.\r","\r","\"Then you can do a few wizzes and get us out of this hole,\" declared the\r","tiny one, with much confidence.\r","\r","\"I could if I happened to be a real wizard,\" returned the master sadly.\r","\"But I'm not, my piggy-wees; I'm a humbug wizard.\"\r","\r","\"Nonsense!\" cried several of the piglets, together.\r","\r","\"You can ask Dorothy,\" said the little man, in an injured tone.\r","\r","\"It's true enough,\" returned the girl, earnestly. \"Our friend Oz is\r","merely a humbug wizard, for he once proved it to me. He can do several\r","very wonderful things--if he knows how. But he can't wiz a single thing\r","if he hasn't the tools and machinery to work with.\"\r","\r","\"Thank you, my dear, for doing me justice,\" responded the Wizard,\r","gratefully. \"To be accused of being a real wizard, when I'm not, is a\r","slander I will not tamely submit to. But I am one of the greatest humbug\r","wizards that ever lived, and you will realize this when we have all\r","starved together and our bones are scattered over the floor of this\r","lonely cave.\"\r","\r","\"I don't believe we'll realize anything, when it comes to that,\"\r","remarked Dorothy, who had been deep in thought. \"But I'm not going to\r","scatter my bones just yet, because I need them, and you prob'ly need\r","yours, too.\"\r","\r","\"We are helpless to escape,\" sighed the Wizard.\r","\r","\"_We_ may be helpless,\" answered Dorothy, smiling at him, \"but there are\r","others who can do more than we can. Cheer up, friends. I'm sure Ozma\r","will help us.\"\r","\r","\"Ozma!\" exclaimed the Wizard. \"Who is Ozma?\"\r","\r","\"The girl that rules the marvelous Land of Oz,\" was the reply. \"She's a\r","friend of mine, for I met her in the Land of Ev, not long ago, and went\r","to Oz with her.\"\r","\r","\"For the second time?\" asked the Wizard, with great interest.\r","\r","\"Yes. The first time I went to Oz I found you there, ruling the Emerald\r","City. After you went up in a balloon, and escaped us, I got back to\r","Kansas by means of a pair of magical silver shoes.\"\r","\r","\"I remember those shoes,\" said the little man, nodding. \"They once\r","belonged to the Wicked Witch. Have you them here with you?\"\r","\r","\"No; I lost them somewhere in the air,\" explained the child. \"But the\r","second time I went to the Land of Oz I owned the Nome King's Magic Belt,\r","which is much more powerful than were the Silver Shoes.\"\r","\r","\"Where is that Magic Belt?\" enquired the Wizard, who had listened with\r","great interest.\r","\r","\"Ozma has it; for its powers won't work in a common, ordinary country\r","like the United States. Anyone in a fairy country like the Land of Oz\r","can do anything with it; so I left it with my friend the Princess Ozma,\r","who used it to wish me in Australia with Uncle Henry.\"\r","\r","\"And were you?\" asked Zeb, astonished at what he heard.\r","\r","\"Of course; in just a jiffy. And Ozma has an enchanted picture hanging\r","in her room that shows her the exact scene where any of her friends may\r","be, at any time she chooses. All she has to do is to say: 'I wonder what\r","So-and-so is doing,' and at once the picture shows where her friend is\r","and what the friend is doing. That's _real_ magic, Mr. Wizard; isn't it?\r","Well, every day at four o'clock Ozma has promised to look at me in that\r","picture, and if I am in need of help I am to make her a certain sign and\r","she will put on the Nome King's Magic Belt and wish me to be with her in\r","Oz.\"\r","\r","\"Do you mean that Princess Ozma will see this cave in her enchanted\r","picture, and see all of us here, and what we are doing?\" demanded Zeb.\r","\r","\"Of course; when it is four o'clock,\" she replied, with a laugh at his\r","startled expression.\r","\r","\"And when you make a sign she will bring you to her in the Land of Oz?\"\r","continued the boy.\r","\r","\"That's it, exactly; by means of the Magic Belt.\"\r","\r","\"Then,\" said the Wizard, \"you will be saved, little Dorothy; and I am\r","very glad of it. The rest of us will die much more cheerfully when we\r","know you have escaped our sad fate.\"\r","\r","\"_I_ won't die cheerfully!\" protested the kitten. \"There's nothing\r","cheerful about dying that I could ever see, although they say a cat has\r","nine lives, and so must die nine times.\"\r","\r","\"Have you ever died yet?\" enquired the boy.\r","\r","\"No, and I'm not anxious to begin,\" said Eureka.\r","\r","\"Don't worry, dear,\" Dorothy exclaimed, \"I'll hold you in my arms, and\r","take you with me.\"\r","\r","\"Take us, too!\" cried the nine tiny piglets, all in one breath.\r","\r","\"Perhaps I can,\" answered Dorothy. \"I'll try.\"\r","\r","\"Couldn't you manage to hold me in your arms?\" asked the cab-horse.\r","\r","Dorothy laughed.\r","\r","\"I'll do better than that,\" she promised, \"for I can easily save you\r","all, once I am myself in the Land of Oz.\"\r","\r","\"How?\" they asked.\r","\r","\"By using the Magic Belt. All I need do is to wish you with me, and\r","there you'll be--safe in the royal palace!\"\r","\r","\"Good!\" cried Zeb.\r","\r","\"I built that palace, and the Emerald City, too,\" remarked the Wizard,\r","in a thoughtful tone, \"and I'd like to see them again, for I was very\r","happy among the Munchkins and Winkies and Quadlings and Gillikins.\"\r","\r","\"Who are they?\" asked the boy.\r","\r","\"The four nations that inhabit the Land of Oz,\" was the reply. \"I wonder\r","if they would treat me nicely if I went there again.\"\r","\r","\"Of course they would!\" declared Dorothy. \"They are still proud of their\r","former Wizard, and often speak of you kindly.\"\r","\r","\"Do you happen to know whatever became of the Tin Woodman and the\r","Scarecrow?\" he enquired.\r","\r","\"They live in Oz yet,\" said the girl, \"and are very important people.\"\r","\r","\"And the Cowardly Lion?\"\r","\r","\"Oh, he lives there too, with his friend the Hungry Tiger; and Billina\r","is there, because she liked the place better than Kansas, and wouldn't\r","go with me to Australia.\"\r","\r","\"I'm afraid I don't know the Hungry Tiger and Billina,\" said the Wizard,\r","shaking his head. \"Is Billina a girl?\"\r","\r","\"No; she's a yellow hen, and a great friend of mine. You're sure to like\r","Billina, when you know her,\" asserted Dorothy.\r","\r","\"Your friends sound like a menagerie,\" remarked Zeb, uneasily.\r","\"Couldn't you wish me in some safer place than Oz.\"\r","\r","\"Don't worry,\" replied the girl. \"You'll just love the folks in Oz, when\r","you get acquainted. What time is it, Mr. Wizard?\"\r","\r","The little man looked at his watch--a big silver one that he carried in\r","his vest pocket.\r","\r","\"Half-past three,\" he said.\r","\r","\"Then we must wait for half an hour,\" she continued; \"but it won't take\r","long, after that, to carry us all to the Emerald City.\"\r","\r","They sat silently thinking for a time. Then Jim suddenly asked:\r","\r","\"Are there any horses in Oz?\"\r","\r","\"Only one,\" replied Dorothy, \"and he's a sawhorse.\"\r","\r","\"A what?\"\r","\r","\"A sawhorse. Princess Ozma once brought him to life with a witch-powder,\r","when she was a boy.\"\r","\r","\"Was Ozma once a boy?\" asked Zeb, wonderingly.\r","\r","\"Yes; a wicked witch enchanted her, so she could not rule her kingdom.\r","But she's a girl now, and the sweetest, loveliest girl in all the\r","world.\"\r","\r","\"A sawhorse is a thing they saw boards on,\" remarked Jim, with a sniff.\r","\r","\"It is when it's not alive,\" acknowledged the girl. \"But this sawhorse\r","can trot as fast as you can, Jim; and he's very wise, too.\"\r","\r","\"Pah! I'll race the miserable wooden donkey any day in the week!\" cried\r","the cab-horse.\r","\r","Dorothy did not reply to that. She felt that Jim would know more about\r","the Saw-Horse later on.\r","\r","The time dragged wearily enough to the eager watchers, but finally the\r","Wizard announced that four o'clock had arrived, and Dorothy caught up\r","the kitten and began to make the signal that had been agreed upon to the\r","far-away, invisible Ozma.\r","\r","\"Nothing seems to happen,\" said Zeb, doubtfully.\r","\r","\"Oh, we must give Ozma time to put on the Magic Belt,\" replied the girl.\r","\r","She had scarcely spoken the words when she suddenly disappeared from the\r","cave, and with her went the kitten. There had been no sound of any kind\r","and no warning. One moment Dorothy sat beside them with the kitten in\r","her lap, and a moment later the horse, the piglets, the Wizard and the\r","boy were all that remained in the underground prison.\r","\r","[Illustration: DOROTHY MADE THE SIGNAL.]\r","\r","\"I believe we will soon follow her,\" announced the Wizard, in a tone of\r","great relief; \"for I know something about the magic of the fairyland\r","that is called the Land of Oz. Let us be ready, for we may be sent for\r","any minute.\"\r","\r","He put the piglets safely away in his pocket again and then he and Zeb\r","got into the buggy and sat expectantly upon the seat.\r","\r","\"Will it hurt?\" asked the boy, in a voice that trembled a little.\r","\r","\"Not at all,\" replied the Wizard. \"It will all happen as quick as a\r","wink.\"\r","\r","And that was the way it did happen.\r","\r","The cab-horse gave a nervous start and Zeb began to rub his eyes to make\r","sure he was not asleep. For they were in the streets of a beautiful\r","emerald-green city, bathed in a grateful green light that was especially\r","pleasing to their eyes, and surrounded by merry faced people in gorgeous\r","green-and-gold costumes of many extraordinary designs.\r","\r","Before them were the jewel-studded gates of a magnificent palace, and\r","now the gates opened slowly as if inviting them to enter the courtyard,\r","where splendid flowers were blooming and pretty fountains shot their\r","silvery sprays into the air.\r","\r","Zeb shook the reins to rouse the cab-horse from his stupor of amazement,\r","for the people were beginning to gather around and stare at the\r","strangers.\r","\r","\"Gid-dap!\" cried the boy, and at the word Jim slowly trotted into the\r","courtyard and drew the buggy along the jewelled driveway to the great\r","entrance of the royal palace.\r","\r","[Illustration]\r","\r","\r","\r","CHAPTER 15.\r","\r","OLD FRIENDS ARE REUNITED\r","\r","\r","Many servants dressed in handsome uniforms stood ready to welcome the\r","new arrivals, and when the Wizard got out of the buggy a pretty girl in\r","a green gown cried out in surprise:\r","\r","\"Why, it's Oz, the Wonderful Wizard, come back again!\"\r","\r","The little man looked at her closely and then took both the maiden's\r","hands in his and shook them cordially.\r","\r","\"On my word,\" he exclaimed, \"it's little Jellia Jamb--as pert and pretty\r","as ever!\"\r","\r","\"Why not, Mr. Wizard?\" asked Jellia, bowing low. \"But I'm afraid you\r","cannot rule the Emerald City, as you used to, because we now have a\r","beautiful Princess whom everyone loves dearly.\"\r","\r","\"And the people will not willingly part with her,\" added a tall soldier\r","in a Captain-General's uniform.\r","\r","The Wizard turned to look at him.\r","\r","\"Did you not wear green whiskers at one time?\" he asked.\r","\r","\"Yes,\" said the soldier; \"but I shaved them off long ago, and since then\r","I have risen from a private to be the Chief General of the Royal\r","Armies.\"\r","\r","\"That's nice,\" said the little man. \"But I assure you, my good people,\r","that I do not wish to rule the Emerald City,\" he added, earnestly.\r","\r","\"In that case you are very welcome!\" cried all the servants, and it\r","pleased the Wizard to note the respect with which the royal retainers\r","bowed before him. His fame had not been forgotten in the Land of Oz, by\r","any means.\r","\r","\"Where is Dorothy?\" enquired Zeb, anxiously, as he left the buggy and\r","stood beside his friend the little Wizard.\r","\r","\"She is with the Princess Ozma, in the private rooms of the palace,\"\r","replied Jellia Jamb. \"But she has ordered me to make you welcome and to\r","show you to your apartments.\"\r","\r","The boy looked around him with wondering eyes. Such magnificence and\r","wealth as was displayed in this palace was more than he had ever dreamed\r","of, and he could scarcely believe that all the gorgeous glitter was real\r","and not tinsel.\r","\r","\"What's to become of me?\" asked the horse, uneasily. He had seen\r","considerable of life in the cities in his younger days, and knew that\r","this regal palace was no place for him.\r","\r","It perplexed even Jellia Jamb, for a time, to know what to do with the\r","animal. The green maiden was much astonished at the sight of so unusual\r","a creature, for horses were unknown in this Land; but those who lived in\r","the Emerald City were apt to be astonished by queer sights, so after\r","inspecting the cab-horse and noting the mild look in his big eyes the\r","girl decided not to be afraid of him.\r","\r","\"There are no stables here,\" said the Wizard, \"unless some have been\r","built since I went away.\"\r","\r","\"We have never needed them before,\" answered Jellia; \"for the Sawhorse\r","lives in a room of the palace, being much smaller and more natural in\r","appearance than this great beast you have brought with you.\"\r","\r","\"Do you mean that I'm a freak?\" asked Jim, angrily.\r","\r","\"Oh, no,\" she hastened to say, \"there may be many more like you in the\r","place you came from, but in Oz any horse but a Sawhorse is unusual.\"\r","\r","This mollified Jim a little, and after some thought the green maiden\r","decided to give the cab-horse a room in the palace, such a big building\r","having many rooms that were seldom in use.\r","\r","So Zeb unharnessed Jim, and several of the servants then led the horse\r","around to the rear, where they selected a nice large apartment that he\r","could have all to himself.\r","\r","Then Jellia said to the Wizard:\r","\r","\"Your own room--which was back of the great Throne Room--has been vacant\r","ever since you left us. Would you like it again?\"\r","\r","\"Yes, indeed!\" returned the little man. \"It will seem like being at home\r","again, for I lived in that room for many, many years.\"\r","\r","He knew the way to it, and a servant followed him, carrying his satchel.\r","Zeb was also escorted to a room--so grand and beautiful that he almost\r","feared to sit in the chairs or lie upon the bed, lest he might dim their\r","splendor. In the closets he discovered many fancy costumes of rich\r","velvets and brocades, and one of the attendants told him to dress\r","himself in any of the clothes that pleased him and to be prepared to\r","dine with the Princess and Dorothy in an hour's time.\r","\r","Opening from the chamber was a fine bath-room having a marble tub with\r","perfumed water; so the boy, still dazed by the novelty of his\r","surroundings, indulged in a good bath and then selected a maroon velvet\r","costume with silver buttons to replace his own soiled and much worn\r","clothing. There were silk stockings and soft leather slippers with\r","diamond buckles to accompany his new costume, and when he was fully\r","dressed Zeb looked much more dignified and imposing than ever before in\r","his life.\r","\r","He was all ready when an attendant came to escort him to the presence of\r","the Princess; he followed bashfully and was ushered into a room more\r","dainty and attractive than it was splendid. Here he found Dorothy seated\r","beside a young girl so marvelously beautiful that the boy stopped\r","suddenly with a gasp of admiration.\r","\r","But Dorothy sprang up and ran to seize her friend's hand, drawing him\r","impulsively toward the lovely Princess, who smiled most graciously upon\r","her guest. Then the Wizard entered, and his presence relieved the boy's\r","embarrassment. The little man was clothed in black velvet, with many\r","sparkling emerald ornaments decorating his breast; but his bald head and\r","wrinkled features made him appear more amusing than impressive.\r","\r","Ozma had been quite curious to meet the famous man who had built the\r","Emerald City and united the Munchkins, Gillikins, Quadlings and Winkies\r","into one people; so when they were all four seated at the dinner table\r","the Princess said:\r","\r","\"Please tell me, Mr. Wizard, whether you called yourself Oz after this\r","great country, or whether you believe my country is called Oz after you.\r","It is a matter that I have long wished to enquire about, because you are\r","of a strange race and my own name is Ozma. No one, I am sure, is better\r","able to explain this mystery than you.\"\r","\r","\"That is true,\" answered the little Wizard; \"therefore it will give me\r","pleasure to explain my connection with your country. In the first place,\r","I must tell you that I was born in Omaha, and my father, who was a\r","politician, named me Oscar Zoroaster Phadrig Isaac Norman Henkle\r","Emmannuel Ambroise Diggs, Diggs being the last name because he could\r","think of no more to go before it. Taken altogether, it was a dreadfully\r","long name to weigh down a poor innocent child, and one of the hardest\r","lessons I ever learned was to remember my own name. When I grew up I\r","just called myself O. Z., because the other initials were P-I-N-H-E-A-D;\r","and that spelled 'pinhead,' which was a reflection on my intelligence.\"\r","\r","\"Surely no one could blame you for cutting your name short,\" said Ozma,\r","sympathetically. \"But didn't you cut it almost too short?\"\r","\r","\"Perhaps so,\" replied the Wizard. \"When a young man I ran away from home\r","and joined a circus. I used to call myself a Wizard, and do tricks of\r","ventriloquism.\"\r","\r","\"What does that mean?\" asked the Princess.\r","\r","\"Throwing my voice into any object I pleased, to make it appear that the\r","object was speaking instead of me. Also I began to make balloon\r","ascensions. On my balloon and on all the other articles I used in the\r","circus I painted the two initials: 'O. Z.', to show that those things\r","belonged to me.\r","\r","\"One day my balloon ran away with me and brought me across the deserts\r","to this beautiful country. When the people saw me come from the sky they\r","naturally thought me some superior creature, and bowed down before me. I\r","told them I was a Wizard, and showed them some easy tricks that amazed\r","them; and when they saw the initials painted on the balloon they called\r","me Oz.\"\r","\r","\"Now I begin to understand,\" said the Princess, smiling.\r","\r","\"At that time,\" continued the Wizard, busily eating his soup while\r","talking, \"there were four separate countries in this Land, each one of\r","the four being ruled by a Witch. But the people thought my power was\r","greater than that of the Witches; and perhaps the Witches thought so\r","too, for they never dared oppose me. I ordered the Emerald City to be\r","built just where the four countries cornered together, and when it was\r","completed I announced myself the Ruler of the Land of Oz, which included\r","all the four countries of the Munchkins, the Gillikins, the Winkies and\r","the Quadlings. Over this Land I ruled in peace for many years, until I\r","grew old and longed to see my native city once again. So when Dorothy\r","was first blown to this place by a cyclone I arranged to go away with\r","her in a balloon; but the balloon escaped too soon and carried me back\r","alone. After many adventures I reached Omaha, only to find that all my\r","old friends were dead or had moved away. So, having nothing else to do,\r","I joined a circus again, and made my balloon ascensions until the\r","earthquake caught me.\"\r","\r","\"That is quite a history,\" said Ozma; \"but there is a little more\r","history about the Land of Oz that you do not seem to understand--perhaps\r","for the reason that no one ever told it you. Many years before you came\r","here this Land was united under one Ruler, as it is now, and the Ruler's\r","name was always 'Oz', which means in our language 'Great and Good'; or,\r","if the Ruler happened to be a woman, her name was always 'Ozma.' But\r","once upon a time four Witches leagued together to depose the king and\r","rule the four parts of the kingdom themselves; so when the Ruler, my\r","grandfather, was hunting one day, one Wicked Witch named Mombi stole him\r","and carried him away, keeping him a close prisoner. Then the Witches\r","divided up the kingdom, and ruled the four parts of it until you came\r","here. That was why the people were so glad to see you, and why they\r","thought from your initials that you were their rightful ruler.\"\r","\r","\"But, at that time,\" said the Wizard, thoughtfully, \"there were two Good\r","Witches and two Wicked Witches ruling in the land.\"\r","\r","\"Yes,\" replied Ozma, \"because a good Witch had conquered Mombi in the\r","North and Glinda the Good had conquered the evil Witch in the South. But\r","Mombi was still my grandfather's jailor, and afterward my father's\r","jailor. When I was born she transformed me into a boy, hoping that no\r","one would ever recognize me and know that I was the rightful Princess of\r","the Land of Oz. But I escaped from her and am now the Ruler of my\r","people.\"\r","\r","\"I am very glad of that,\" said the Wizard, \"and hope you will consider\r","me one of your most faithful and devoted subjects.\"\r","\r","\"We owe a great deal to the Wonderful Wizard,\" continued the Princess,\r","\"for it was you who built this splendid Emerald City.\"\r","\r","\"Your people built it,\" he answered. \"I only bossed the job, as we say\r","in Omaha.\"\r","\r","\"But you ruled it wisely and well for many years,\" said she, \"and made\r","the people proud of your magical art. So, as you are now too old to\r","wander abroad and work in a circus, I offer you a home here as long as\r","you live. You shall be the Official Wizard of my kingdom, and be treated\r","with every respect and consideration.\"\r","\r","\"I accept your kind offer with gratitude, gracious Princess,\" the little\r","man said, in a soft voice, and they could all see that tear-drops were\r","standing in his keen old eyes. It meant a good deal to him to secure a\r","home like this.\r","\r","\"He's only a humbug Wizard, though,\" said Dorothy, smiling at him.\r","\r","\"And that is the safest kind of a Wizard to have,\" replied Ozma,\r","promptly.\r","\r","\"Oz can do some good tricks, humbug or no humbug,\" announced Zeb, who\r","was now feeling more at ease.\r","\r","\"He shall amuse us with his tricks tomorrow,\" said the Princess. \"I have\r","sent messengers to summon all of Dorothy's old friends to meet her and\r","give her welcome, and they ought to arrive very soon, now.\"\r","\r","Indeed, the dinner was no sooner finished than in rushed the Scarecrow,\r","to hug Dorothy in his padded arms and tell her how glad he was to see\r","her again. The Wizard was also most heartily welcomed by the straw man,\r","who was an important personage in the Land of Oz.\r","\r","\"How are your brains?\" enquired the little humbug, as he grasped the\r","soft, stuffed hands of his old friend.\r","\r","\"Working finely,\" answered the Scarecrow. \"I'm very certain, Oz, that\r","you gave me the best brains in the world, for I can think with them day\r","and night, when all other brains are fast asleep.\"\r","\r","[Illustration: DOROTHY AND OZMA.]\r","\r","\"How long did you rule the Emerald City, after I left here?\" was the\r","next question.\r","\r","\"Quite awhile, until I was conquered by a girl named General Jinjur. But\r","Ozma soon conquered her, with the help of Glinda the Good, and after\r","that I went to live with Nick Chopper, the Tin Woodman.\"\r","\r","Just then a loud cackling was heard outside; and, when a servant threw\r","open the door with a low bow, a yellow hen strutted in. Dorothy sprang\r","forward and caught the fluffy fowl in her arms, uttering at the same\r","time a glad cry.\r","\r","\"Oh, Billina!\" she said; \"how fat and sleek you've grown.\"\r","\r","\"Why shouldn't I?\" asked the hen, in a sharp, clear voice. \"I live on\r","the fat of the land--don't I, Ozma?\"\r","\r","\"You have everything you wish for,\" said the Princess.\r","\r","Around Billina's neck was a string of beautiful pearls, and on her legs\r","were bracelets of emeralds. She nestled herself comfortably in Dorothy's\r","lap until the kitten gave a snarl of jealous anger and leaped up with a\r","sharp claw fiercely bared to strike Billina a blow. But the little girl\r","gave the angry kitten such a severe cuff that it jumped down again\r","without daring to scratch.\r","\r","\"How horrid of you, Eureka!\" cried Dorothy. \"Is that the way to treat my\r","friends?\"\r","\r","\"You have queer friends, seems to me,\" replied the kitten, in a surly\r","tone.\r","\r","\"Seems to me the same way,\" said Billina, scornfully, \"if that beastly\r","cat is one of them.\"\r","\r","\"Look here!\" said Dorothy, sternly. \"I won't have any quarrelling in the\r","Land of Oz, I can tell you! Everybody lives in peace here, and loves\r","everybody else; and unless you two, Billina and Eureka, make up and be\r","friends, I'll take my Magic Belt and wish you both home again,\r","_immejitly_. So, there!\"\r","\r","They were both much frightened at the threat, and promised meekly to be\r","good. But it was never noticed that they became very warm friends, for\r","all of that.\r","\r","And now the Tin Woodman arrived, his body most beautifully\r","nickle-plated, so that it shone splendidly in the brilliant light of the\r","room. The Tin Woodman loved Dorothy most tenderly, and welcomed with joy\r","the return of the little old Wizard.\r","\r","\"Sir,\" said he to the latter, \"I never can thank you enough for the\r","excellent heart you once gave me. It has made me many friends, I assure\r","you, and it beats as kindly and lovingly today as it ever did.\"\r","\r","\"I'm glad to hear that,\" said the Wizard. \"I was afraid it would get\r","moldy in that tin body of yours.\"\r","\r","\"Not at all,\" returned Nick Chopper. \"It keeps finely, being preserved\r","in my air-tight chest.\"\r","\r","Zeb was a little shy when first introduced to these queer people; but\r","they were so friendly and sincere that he soon grew to admire them very\r","much, even finding some good qualities in the yellow hen. But he became\r","nervous again when the next visitor was announced.\r","\r","\"This,\" said Princess Ozma, \"is my friend Mr. H. M. Woggle-Bug, T. E.,\r","who assisted me one time when I was in great distress, and is now the\r","Dean of the Royal College of Athletic Science.\"\r","\r","\"Ah,\" said the Wizard; \"I'm pleased to meet so distinguished a\r","personage.\"\r","\r","\"H. M.,\" said the Woggle-Bug, pompously, \"means Highly Magnified; and T.\r","E. means Thoroughly Educated. I am, in reality, a very big bug, and\r","doubtless the most intelligent being in all this broad domain.\"\r","\r","\"How well you disguise it,\" said the Wizard. \"But I don't doubt your\r","word in the least.\"\r","\r","\"Nobody doubts it, sir,\" replied the Woggle-Bug, and drawing a book from\r","its pocket the strange insect turned its back on the company and sat\r","down in a corner to read.\r","\r","Nobody minded this rudeness, which might have seemed more impolite in\r","one less thoroughly educated; so they straightway forgot him and joined\r","in a merry conversation that kept them well amused until bed-time\r","arrived.\r","\r","[Illustration]\r","\r","\r","\r","\r","CHAPTER 16.\r","\r","JIM, THE CAB-HORSE\r","\r","\r","Jim the Cab-horse found himself in possession of a large room with a\r","green marble floor and carved marble wainscoting, which was so stately\r","in its appearance that it would have awed anyone else. Jim accepted it\r","as a mere detail, and at his command the attendants gave his coat a good\r","rubbing, combed his mane and tail, and washed his hoofs and fetlocks.\r","Then they told him dinner would be served directly and he replied that\r","they could not serve it too quickly to suit his convenience. First they\r","brought him a steaming bowl of soup, which the horse eyed in dismay.\r","\r","\"Take that stuff away!\" he commanded. \"Do you take me for a\r","salamander?\"\r","\r","They obeyed at once, and next served a fine large turbot on a silver\r","platter, with drawn gravey poured over it.\r","\r","\"Fish!\" cried Jim, with a sniff. \"Do you take me for a tom-cat? Away\r","with it!\"\r","\r","The servants were a little discouraged, but soon they brought in a great\r","tray containing two dozen nicely roasted quail on toast.\r","\r","\"Well, well!\" said the horse, now thoroughly provoked. \"Do you take me\r","for a weasel? How stupid and ignorant you are, in the Land of Oz, and\r","what dreadful things you feed upon! Is there nothing that is decent to\r","eat in this palace?\"\r","\r","The trembling servants sent for the Royal Steward, who came in haste and\r","said:\r","\r","\"What would your Highness like for dinner?\"\r","\r","\"Highness!\" repeated Jim, who was unused to such titles.\r","\r","\"You are at least six feet high, and that is higher than any other\r","animal in this country,\" said the Steward.\r","\r","\"Well, my Highness would like some oats,\" declared the horse.\r","\r","\"Oats? We have no whole oats,\" the Steward replied, with much\r","defference. \"But there is any quantity of oatmeal, which we often cook\r","for breakfast. Oatmeal is a breakfast dish,\" added the Steward, humbly.\r","\r","\"I'll make it a dinner dish,\" said Jim. \"Fetch it on, but don't cook it,\r","as you value your life.\"\r","\r","You see, the respect shown the worn-out old cab-horse made him a little\r","arrogant, and he forgot he was a guest, never having been treated\r","otherwise than as a servant since the day he was born, until his arrival\r","in the Land of Oz. But the royal attendants did not heed the animal's\r","ill temper. They soon mixed a tub of oatmeal with a little water, and\r","Jim ate it with much relish.\r","\r","Then the servants heaped a lot of rugs upon the floor and the old horse\r","slept on the softest bed he had ever known in his life.\r","\r","In the morning, as soon as it was daylight, he resolved to take a walk\r","and try to find some grass for breakfast; so he ambled calmly through\r","the handsome arch of the doorway, turned the corner of the palace,\r","wherein all seemed asleep, and came face to face with the Sawhorse.\r","\r","Jim stopped abruptly, being startled and amazed. The Sawhorse stopped at\r","the same time and stared at the other with its queer protruding eyes,\r","which were mere knots in the log that formed its body. The legs of the\r","Sawhorse were four sticks driven into holes bored in the log; its tail\r","was a small branch that had been left by accident and its mouth a place\r","chopped in one end of the body which projected a little and served as\r","a head. The ends of the wooden legs were shod with plates of solid gold,\r","and the saddle of the Princess Ozma, which was of red leather set with\r","sparkling diamonds, was strapped to the clumsy body.\r","\r","[Illustration: \"FOR GOODNESS SAKE, WHAT SORT OF A BEING ARE YOU?\"]\r","\r","Jim's eyes stuck out as much as those of the Sawhorse, and he stared at\r","the creature with his ears erect and his long head drawn back until it\r","rested against his arched neck.\r","\r","In this comical position the two horses circled slowly around each other\r","for a while, each being unable to realize what the singular thing might\r","be which it now beheld for the first time. Then Jim exclaimed:\r","\r","\"For goodness sake, what sort of a being are you?\"\r","\r","\"I'm a Sawhorse,\" replied the other.\r","\r","\"Oh; I believe I've heard of you,\" said the cab-horse; \"but you are\r","unlike anything that I expected to see.\"\r","\r","\"I do not doubt it,\" the Sawhorse observed, with a tone of pride. \"I am\r","considered quite unusual.\"\r","\r","\"You are, indeed. But a rickety wooden thing like you has no right to be\r","alive.\"\r","\r","\"I couldn't help it,\" returned the other, rather crestfallen. \"Ozma\r","sprinkled me with a magic powder, and I just had to live. I know I'm not\r","much account; but I'm the only horse in all the Land of Oz, so they\r","treat me with great respect.\"\r","\r","\"You, a horse!\"\r","\r","\"Oh, not a real one, of course. There are no real horses here at all.\r","But I'm a splendid imitation of one.\"\r","\r","Jim gave an indignant neigh.\r","\r","\"Look at me!\" he cried. \"Behold a real horse!\"\r","\r","The wooden animal gave a start, and then examined the other intently.\r","\r","\"Is it possible that you are a Real Horse?\" he murmured.\r","\r","\"Not only possible, but true,\" replied Jim, who was gratified by the\r","impression he had created. \"It is proved by my fine points. For example,\r","look at the long hairs on my tail, with which I can whisk away the\r","flies.\"\r","\r","\"The flies never trouble me,\" said the Saw-Horse.\r","\r","\"And notice my great strong teeth, with which I nibble the grass.\"\r","\r","\"It is not necessary for me to eat,\" observed the Saw-horse.\r","\r","\"Also examine my broad chest, which enables me to draw deep, full\r","breaths,\" said Jim, proudly.\r","\r","\"I have no need to breathe,\" returned the other.\r","\r","\"No; you miss many pleasures,\" remarked the cab-horse, pityingly. \"You\r","do not know the relief of brushing away a fly that has bitten you, nor\r","the delight of eating delicious food, nor the satisfaction of drawing a\r","long breath of fresh, pure air. You may be an imitation of a horse, but\r","you're a mighty poor one.\"\r","\r","\"Oh, I cannot hope ever to be like you,\" sighed the Sawhorse. \"But I am\r","glad to meet at last a Real Horse. You are certainly the most beautiful\r","creature I ever beheld.\"\r","\r","This praise won Jim completely. To be called beautiful was a novelty in\r","his experience. Said he:\r","\r","\"Your chief fault, my friend, is in being made of wood, and that I\r","suppose you cannot help. Real horses, like myself, are made of flesh and\r","blood and bones.\"\r","\r","\"I can see the bones all right,\" replied the Sawhorse, \"and they are\r","admirable and distinct. Also I can see the flesh. But the blood, I\r","suppose, is tucked away inside.\"\r","\r","\"Exactly,\" said Jim.\r","\r","\"What good is it?\" asked the Sawhorse.\r","\r","Jim did not know, but he would not tell the Sawhorse that.\r","\r","\"If anything cuts me,\" he replied, \"the blood runs out to show where I\r","am cut. You, poor thing! cannot even bleed when you are hurt.\"\r","\r","\"But I am never hurt,\" said the Sawhorse. \"Once in a while I get broken\r","up some, but I am easily repaired and put in good order again. And I\r","never feel a break or a splinter in the least.\"\r","\r","Jim was almost tempted to envy the wooden horse for being unable to feel\r","pain; but the creature was so absurdly unnatural that he decided he\r","would not change places with it under any circumstances.\r","\r","\"How did you happen to be shod with gold?\" he asked.\r","\r","\"Princess Ozma did that,\" was the reply; \"and it saves my legs from\r","wearing out. We've had a good many adventures together, Ozma and I, and\r","she likes me.\"\r","\r","The cab-horse was about to reply when suddenly he gave a start and a\r","neigh of terror and stood trembling like a leaf. For around the corner\r","had come two enormous savage beasts, treading so lightly that they were\r","upon him before he was aware of their presence. Jim was in the act of\r","plunging down the path to escape when the Sawhorse cried out:\r","\r","\"Stop, my brother! Stop, Real Horse! These are friends, and will do you\r","no harm.\"\r","\r","Jim hesitated, eyeing the beasts fearfully. One was an enormous Lion\r","with clear, intelligent eyes, a tawney mane bushy and well kept, and a\r","body like yellow plush. The other was a great Tiger with purple stripes\r","around his lithe body, powerful limbs, and eyes that showed through the\r","half closed lids like coals of fire. The huge forms of these monarchs of\r","the forest and jungle were enough to strike terror to the stoutest\r","heart, and it is no wonder Jim was afraid to face them.\r","\r","But the Sawhorse introduced the stranger in a calm tone, saying,\r","\r","\"This, noble Horse, is my friend the Cowardly Lion, who is the valiant\r","King of the Forest, but at the same time a faithful vassal of Princess\r","Ozma. And this is the Hungry Tiger, the terror of the jungle, who longs\r","to devour fat babies but is prevented by his conscience from doing so.\r","These royal beasts are both warm friends of little Dorothy and have come\r","to the Emerald City this morning to welcome her to our fairyland.\"\r","\r","Hearing these words Jim resolved to conquer his alarm. He bowed his head\r","with as much dignity as he could muster toward the savage looking\r","beasts, who in return nodded in a friendly way.\r","\r","\"Is not the Real Horse a beautiful animal?\" asked the Sawhorse\r","admiringly.\r","\r","\"That is doubtless a matter of taste,\" returned the Lion. \"In the forest\r","he would be thought ungainly, because his face is stretched out and his\r","neck is uselessly long. His joints, I notice, are swollen and overgrown,\r","and he lacks flesh and is old in years.\"\r","\r","\"And dreadfully tough,\" added the Hungry Tiger, in a sad voice. \"My\r","conscience would never permit me to eat so tough a morsel as the Real\r","Horse.\"\r","\r","\"I'm glad of that,\" said Jim; \"for I, also, have a conscience, and it\r","tells me not to crush in your skull with a blow of my powerful hoof.\"\r","\r","If he thought to frighten the striped beast by such language he was\r","mistaken. The Tiger seemed to smile, and winked one eye slowly.\r","\r","\"You have a good conscience, friend Horse,\" it said, \"and if you attend\r","to its teachings it will do much to protect you from harm. Some day I\r","will let you try to crush in my skull, and afterward you will know more\r","about tigers than you do now.\"\r","\r","\"Any friend of Dorothy,\" remarked the Cowardly Lion, \"must be our\r","friend, as well. So let us cease this talk of skull crushing and\r","converse upon more pleasant subjects. Have you breakfasted, Sir Horse?\"\r","\r","\"Not yet,\" replied Jim. \"But here is plenty of excellent clover, so if\r","you will excuse me I will eat now.\"\r","\r","\"He's a vegetarian,\" remarked the Tiger, as the horse began to munch the\r","clover. \"If I could eat grass I would not need a conscience, for nothing\r","could then tempt me to devour babies and lambs.\"\r","\r","Just then Dorothy, who had risen early and heard the voices of the\r","animals, ran out to greet her old friends. She hugged both the Lion and\r","the Tiger with eager delight, but seemed to love the King of Beasts a\r","little better than she did his hungry friend, having known him longer.\r","\r","By the time they had indulged in a good talk and Dorothy had told them\r","all about the awful earthquake and her recent adventures, the breakfast\r","bell rang from the palace and the little girl went inside to join her\r","human comrades. As she entered the great hall a voice called out, in a\r","rather harsh tone:\r","\r","\"What! are _you_ here again?\"\r","\r","\"Yes, I am,\" she answered, looking all around to see where the voice\r","came from.\r","\r","\"What brought you back?\" was the next question, and Dorothy's eye rested\r","on an antlered head hanging on the wall just over the fireplace, and\r","caught its lips in the act of moving.\r","\r","\"Good gracious!\" she exclaimed. \"I thought you were stuffed.\"\r","\r","\"So I am,\" replied the head. \"But once on a time I was part of the Gump,\r","which Ozma sprinkled with the Powder of Life. I was then for a time the\r","Head of the finest Flying Machine that was ever known to exist, and we\r","did many wonderful things. Afterward the Gump was taken apart and I was\r","put back on this wall; but I can still talk when I feel in the mood,\r","which is not often.\"\r","\r","\"It's very strange,\" said the girl. \"What were you when you were first\r","alive?\"\r","\r","\"That I have forgotten,\" replied the Gump's Head, \"and I do not think it\r","is of much importance. But here comes Ozma; so I'd better hush up, for\r","the Princess doesn't like me to chatter since she changed her name from\r","Tip to Ozma.\"\r","\r","Just then the girlish Ruler of Oz opened the door and greeted Dorothy\r","with a good-morning kiss. The little Princess seemed fresh and rosy and\r","in good spirits.\r","\r","\"Breakfast is served, dear,\" she said, \"and I am hungry. So don't let us\r","keep it waiting a single minute.\"\r","\r","[Illustration]\r","\r","[Illustration: JIM STOOD TREMBLING LIKE A LEAF.]\r","\r","\r","\r","\r","CHAPTER 17.\r","\r","THE NINE TINY PIGLETS\r","\r","\r","After breakfast Ozma announced that she had ordered a holiday to be\r","observed throughout the Emerald City, in honor of her visitors. The\r","people had learned that their old Wizard had returned to them and all\r","were anxious to see him again, for he had always been a rare favorite.\r","So first there was to be a grand procession through the streets, after\r","which the little old man was requested to perform some of his wizardries\r","in the great Throne Room of the palace. In the afternoon there were to\r","be games and races.\r","\r","The procession was very imposing. First came the Imperial Cornet Band of\r","Oz, dressed in emerald velvet uniforms with slashes of pea-green satin\r","and buttons of immense cut emeralds. They played the National air\r","called \"The Oz Spangled Banner,\" and behind them were the standard\r","bearers with the Royal flag. This flag was divided into four quarters,\r","one being colored sky-blue, another pink, a third lavender and a fourth\r","white. In the center was a large emerald-green star, and all over the\r","four quarters were sewn spangles that glittered beautifully in the\r","sunshine. The colors represented the four countries of Oz, and the green\r","star the Emerald City.\r","\r","Just behind the royal standard-bearers came the Princess Ozma in her\r","royal chariot, which was of gold encrusted with emeralds and diamonds\r","set in exquisite designs. The chariot was drawn on this occasion by the\r","Cowardly Lion and the Hungry Tiger, who were decorated with immense pink\r","and blue bows. In the chariot rode Ozma and Dorothy, the former in\r","splendid raiment and wearing her royal coronet, while the little Kansas\r","girl wore around her waist the Magic Belt she had once captured from the\r","Nome King.\r","\r","Following the chariot came the Scarecrow mounted on the Sawhorse, and\r","the people cheered him almost as loudly as they did their lovely Ruler.\r","Behind him stalked with regular, jerky steps, the famous machine-man\r","called Tik-tok, who had been wound up by Dorothy for the occasion.\r","Tik-tok moved by clockwork, and was made all of burnished copper. He\r","really belonged to the Kansas girl, who had much respect for his\r","thoughts after they had been properly wound and set going; but as the\r","copper man would be useless in any place but a fairy country Dorothy had\r","left him in charge of Ozma, who saw that he was suitably cared for.\r","\r","There followed another band after this, which was called the Royal Court\r","Band, because the members all lived in the palace. They wore white\r","uniforms with real diamond buttons and played \"What is Oz without Ozma\"\r","very sweetly.\r","\r","Then came Professor Woggle-Bug, with a group of students from the Royal\r","College of Scientific Athletics. The boys wore long hair and striped\r","sweaters and yelled their college yell every other step they took, to\r","the great satisfaction of the populace, which was glad to have this\r","evidence that their lungs were in good condition.\r","\r","The brilliantly polished Tin Woodman marched next, at the head of the\r","Royal Army of Oz which consisted of twenty-eight officers, from Generals\r","down to Captains. There were no privates in the army because all were so\r","courageous and skillful that they had been promoted one by one until\r","there were no privates left. Jim and the buggy followed, the old\r","cab-horse being driven by Zeb while the Wizard stood up on the seat and\r","bowed his bald head right and left in answer to the cheers of the\r","people, who crowded thick about him.\r","\r","Taken altogether the procession was a grand success, and when it had\r","returned to the palace the citizens crowded into the great Throne Room\r","to see the Wizard perform his tricks.\r","\r","The first thing the little humbug did was to produce a tiny white piglet\r","from underneath his hat and pretend to pull it apart, making two. This\r","act he repeated until all of the nine tiny piglets were visible, and\r","they were so glad to get out of his pocket that they ran around in a\r","very lively manner. The pretty little creatures would have been a\r","novelty anywhere, so the people were as amazed and delighted at their\r","appearance as even the Wizard could have desired. When he had made them\r","all disappear again Ozma declared she was sorry they were gone, for she\r","wanted one of them to pet and play with. So the Wizard pretended to take\r","one of the piglets out of the hair of the Princess (while really he\r","slyly took it from his inside pocket) and Ozma smiled joyously as the\r","creature nestled in her arms, and she promised to have an emerald collar\r","made for its fat neck and to keep the little squealer always at hand to\r","amuse her.\r","\r","Afterward it was noticed that the Wizard always performed his famous\r","trick with eight piglets, but it seemed to please the people just as\r","well as if there had been nine of them.\r","\r","In his little room back of the Throne Room the Wizard had found a lot of\r","things he had left behind him when he went away in the balloon, for no\r","one had occupied the apartment in his absence. There was enough material\r","there to enable him to prepare several new tricks which he had learned\r","from some of the jugglers in the circus, and he had passed part of the\r","night in getting them ready. So he followed the trick of the nine tiny\r","piglets with several other wonderful feats that greatly delighted his\r","audience and the people did not seem to care a bit whether the little\r","man was a humbug Wizard or not, so long as he succeeded in amusing them.\r","They applauded all his tricks and at the end of the performance begged\r","him earnestly not to go away again and leave them.\r","\r","\"In that case,\" said the little man, gravely, \"I will cancel all of my\r","engagements before the crowned heads of Europe and America and devote\r","myself to the people of Oz, for I love you all so well that I can deny\r","you nothing.\"\r","\r","After the people had been dismissed with this promise our friends joined\r","Princess Ozma at an elaborate luncheon in the palace, where even the\r","Tiger and the Lion were sumptuously fed and Jim the Cab-horse ate his\r","oatmeal out of a golden bowl with seven rows of rubies, sapphires and\r","diamonds set around the rim of it.\r","\r","In the afternoon they all went to a great field outside the city gates\r","where the games were to be held. There was a beautiful canopy for Ozma\r","and her guests to sit under and watch the people run races and jump and\r","wrestle. You may be sure the folks of Oz did their best with such a\r","distinguished company watching them, and finally Zeb offered to wrestle\r","with a little Munchkin who seemed to be the champion. In appearance he\r","was twice as old as Zeb, for he had long pointed whiskers and wore a\r","peaked hat with little bells all around the brim of it, which tinkled\r","gaily as he moved. But although the Munchkin was hardly tall enough to\r","come to Zeb's shoulder he was so strong and clever that he laid the boy\r","three times on his back with apparent ease.\r","\r","Zeb was greatly astonished at his defeat, and when the pretty Princess\r","joined her people in laughing at him he proposed a boxing-match with the\r","Munchkin, to which the little Ozite readily agreed. But the first time\r","that Zeb managed to give him a sharp box on the ears the Munchkin sat\r","down upon the ground and cried until the tears ran down his whiskers,\r","because he had been hurt. This made Zeb laugh, in turn, and the boy\r","felt comforted to find that Ozma laughed as merrily at her weeping\r","subject as she had at him.\r","\r","Just then the Scarecrow proposed a race between the Sawhorse and the\r","Cab-horse; and although all the others were delighted at the suggestion\r","the Sawhorse drew back, saying:\r","\r","\"Such a race would not be fair.\"\r","\r","\"Of course not,\" added Jim, with a touch of scorn; \"those little wooden\r","legs of yours are not half as long as my own.\"\r","\r","\"It isn't that,\" said the Sawhorse, modestly; \"but I never tire, and you\r","do.\"\r","\r","\"Bah!\" cried Jim, looking with great disdain at the other; \"do you\r","imagine for an instant that such a shabby imitation of a horse as you\r","are can run as fast as I?\"\r","\r","\"I don't know, I'm sure,\" replied the Sawhorse.\r","\r","\"That is what we are trying to find out,\" remarked the Scarecrow. \"The\r","object of a race is to see who can win it--or at least that is what my\r","excellent brains think.\"\r","\r","\"Once, when I was young,\" said Jim, \"I was a race horse, and defeated\r","all who dared run against me. I was born in Kentucky, you know, where\r","all the best and most aristocratic horses come from.\"\r","\r","\"But you're old, now, Jim,\" suggested Zeb.\r","\r","\"Old! Why, I feel like a colt today,\" replied Jim. \"I only wish there\r","was a real horse here for me to race with. I'd show the people a fine\r","sight, I can tell you.\"\r","\r","\"Then why not race with the Sawhorse?\" enquired the Scarecrow.\r","\r","\"He's afraid,\" said Jim.\r","\r","\"Oh, no,\" answered the Sawhorse. \"I merely said it wasn't fair. But if\r","my friend the Real Horse is willing to undertake the race I am quite\r","ready.\"\r","\r","So they unharnessed Jim and took the saddle off the Sawhorse, and the\r","two queerly matched animals were stood side by side for the start.\r","\r","\"When I say 'Go!'\" Zeb called to them, \"you must dig out and race until\r","you reach those three trees you see over yonder. Then circle 'round them\r","and come back again. The first one that passes the place where the\r","Princess sits shall be named the winner. Are you ready?\"\r","\r","\"I suppose I ought to give the wooden dummy a good start of me,\" growled\r","Jim.\r","\r","\"Never mind that,\" said the Sawhorse. \"I'll do the best I can.\"\r","\r","\"Go!\" cried Zeb; and at the word the two horses leaped forward and the\r","race was begun.\r","\r","[Illustration: THE WIZARD TOOK A PIGLET FROM OZMA'S HAIR.]\r","\r","Jim's big hoofs pounded away at a great rate, and although he did not\r","look very graceful he ran in a way to do credit to his Kentucky\r","breeding. But the Sawhorse was swifter than the wind. Its wooden legs\r","moved so fast that their twinkling could scarcely be seen, and\r","although so much smaller than the cab-horse it covered the ground much\r","faster. Before they had reached the trees the Sawhorse was far ahead,\r","and the wooden animal returned to the starting place and was being\r","lustily cheered by the Ozites before Jim came panting up to the canopy\r","where the Princess and her friends were seated.\r","\r","[Illustration: THE HUNGRY TIGER TEACHES JIM A LESSON.]\r","\r","I am sorry to record the fact that Jim was not only ashamed of his\r","defeat but for a moment lost control of his temper. As he looked at the\r","comical face of the Sawhorse he imagined that the creature was laughing\r","at him; so in a fit of unreasonable anger he turned around and made a\r","vicious kick that sent his rival tumbling head over heels upon the\r","ground, and broke off one of its legs and its left ear.\r","\r","An instant later the Tiger crouched and launched its huge body through\r","the air swift and resistless as a ball from a cannon. The beast struck\r","Jim full on his shoulder and sent the astonished cab-horse rolling over\r","and over, amid shouts of delight from the spectators, who had been\r","horrified by the ungracious act he had been guilty of.\r","\r","When Jim came to himself and sat upon his haunches he found the Cowardly\r","Lion crouched on one side of him and the Hungry Tiger on the other, and\r","their eyes were glowing like balls of fire.\r","\r","\"I beg your pardon, I'm sure,\" said Jim, meekly. \"I was wrong to kick\r","the Sawhorse, and I am sorry I became angry at him. He has won the race,\r","and won it fairly; but what can a horse of flesh do against a tireless\r","beast of wood?\"\r","\r","Hearing this apology the Tiger and the Lion stopped lashing their tails\r","and retreated with dignified steps to the side of the Princess.\r","\r","\"No one must injure one of our friends in our presence,\" growled the\r","Lion; and Zeb ran to Jim and whispered that unless he controlled his\r","temper in the future he would probably be torn to pieces.\r","\r","Then the Tin Woodman cut a straight and strong limb from a tree with his\r","gleaming axe and made a new leg and a new ear for the Sawhorse; and when\r","they had been securely fastened in place Princess Ozma took the coronet\r","from her own head and placed it upon that of the winner of the race.\r","Said she:\r","\r","\"My friend, I reward you for your swiftness by proclaiming you Prince of\r","Horses, whether of wood or of flesh; and hereafter all other horses--in\r","the Land of Oz, at least--must be considered imitations, and you the\r","real Champion of your race.\"\r","\r","There was more applause at this, and then Ozma had the jewelled saddle\r","replaced upon the Sawhorse and herself rode the victor back to the city\r","at the head of the grand procession.\r","\r","\"I ought to be a fairy,\" grumbled Jim, as he slowly drew the buggy home;\r","\"for to be just an ordinary horse in a fairy country is to be of no\r","account whatever. It's no place for us, Zeb.\"\r","\r","\"It's lucky we got here, though,\" said the boy; and Jim thought of the\r","dark cave, and agreed with him.\r","\r","[Illustration]\r","\r","\r","\r","\r","CHAPTER 18.\r","\r","THE TRIAL OF EUREKA THE KITTEN\r","\r","\r","Several days of festivity and merry-making followed, for such old\r","friends did not often meet and there was much to be told and talked over\r","between them, and many amusements to be enjoyed in this delightful\r","country.\r","\r","Ozma was happy to have Dorothy beside her, for girls of her own age with\r","whom it was proper for the Princess to associate were very few, and\r","often the youthful Ruler of Oz was lonely for lack of companionship.\r","\r","It was the third morning after Dorothy's arrival, and she was sitting\r","with Ozma and their friends in a reception room, talking over old times,\r","when the Princess said to her maid:\r","\r","\"Please go to my boudoir, Jellia, and get the white piglet I left on the\r","dressing-table. I want to play with it.\"\r","\r","Jellia at once departed on the errand, and she was gone so long that\r","they had almost forgotten her mission when the green robed maiden\r","returned with a troubled face.\r","\r","\"The piglet is not there, your Highness,\" said she.\r","\r","\"Not there!\" exclaimed Ozma. \"Are you sure?\"\r","\r","\"I have hunted in every part of the room,\" the maid replied.\r","\r","\"Was not the door closed?\" asked the Princess.\r","\r","\"Yes, your Highness; I am sure it was; for when I opened it Dorothy's\r","white kitten crept out and ran up the stairs.\"\r","\r","Hearing this, Dorothy and the Wizard exchanged startled glances, for\r","they remembered how often Eureka had longed to eat a piglet. The little\r","girl jumped up at once.\r","\r","\"Come, Ozma,\" she said, anxiously; \"let us go ourselves to search for\r","the piglet.\"\r","\r","So the two went to the dressing-room of the Princess and searched\r","carefully in every corner and among the vases and baskets and ornaments\r","that stood about the pretty boudoir. But not a trace could they find of\r","the tiny creature they sought.\r","\r","Dorothy was nearly weeping, by this time, while Ozma was angry and\r","indignant. When they returned to the others the Princess said:\r","\r","\"There is little doubt that my pretty piglet has been eaten by that\r","horrid kitten, and if that is true the offender must be punished.\"\r","\r","\"I don't b'lieve Eureka would do such a dreadful thing!\" cried Dorothy,\r","much distressed. \"Go and get my kitten, please, Jellia, and we'll hear\r","what she has to say about it.\"\r","\r","The green maiden hastened away, but presently returned and said:\r","\r","\"The kitten will not come. She threatened to scratch my eyes out if I\r","touched her.\"\r","\r","\"Where is she?\" asked Dorothy.\r","\r","\"Under the bed in your own room,\" was the reply.\r","\r","So Dorothy ran to her room and found the kitten under the bed.\r","\r","\"Come here, Eureka!\" she said.\r","\r","\"I won't,\" answered the kitten, in a surly voice.\r","\r","\"Oh, Eureka! Why are you so bad?\"\r","\r","The kitten did not reply.\r","\r","\"If you don't come to me, right away,\" continued Dorothy, getting\r","provoked, \"I'll take my Magic Belt and wish you in the Country of the\r","Gurgles.\"\r","\r","\"Why do you want me?\" asked Eureka, disturbed by this threat.\r","\r","\"You must go to Princess Ozma. She wants to talk to you.\"\r","\r","\"All right,\" returned the kitten, creeping out. \"I'm not afraid of\r","Ozma--or anyone else.\"\r","\r","Dorothy carried her in her arms back to where the others sat in grieved\r","and thoughtful silence.\r","\r","\"Tell me, Eureka,\" said the Princess, gently: \"did you eat my pretty\r","piglet?\"\r","\r","\"I won't answer such a foolish question,\" asserted Eureka, with a snarl.\r","\r","\"Oh, yes you will, dear,\" Dorothy declared. \"The piglet is gone, and you\r","ran out of the room when Jellia opened the door. So, if you are\r","innocent, Eureka, you must tell the Princess how you came to be in her\r","room, and what has become of the piglet.\"\r","\r","\"Who accuses me?\" asked the kitten, defiantly.\r","\r","\"No one,\" answered Ozma. \"Your actions alone accuse you. The fact is\r","that I left my little pet in my dressing-room lying asleep upon the\r","table; and you must hove stolen in without my knowing it. When next the\r","door was opened you ran out and hid yourself--and the piglet was gone.\"\r","\r","\"That's none of my business,\" growled the kitten.\r","\r","\"Don't be impudent, Eureka,\" admonished Dorothy.\r","\r","\"It is you who are impudent,\" said Eureka, \"for accusing me of such a\r","crime when you can't prove it except by guessing.\"\r","\r","Ozma was now greatly incensed by the kitten's conduct. She summoned her\r","Captain-General, and when the long, lean officer appeared she said:\r","\r","\"Carry this cat away to prison, and keep her in safe confinement until\r","she is tried by law for the crime of murder.\"\r","\r","So the Captain-General took Eureka from the arms of the now weeping\r","Dorothy and in spite of the kitten's snarls and scratches carried it\r","away to prison.\r","\r","\"What shall we do now?\" asked the Scarecrow, with a sigh, for such a\r","crime had cast a gloom over all the company.\r","\r","\"I will summon the Court to meet in the Throne Room at three o'clock,\"\r","replied Ozma. \"I myself will be the judge, and the kitten shall have a\r","fair trial.\"\r","\r","\"What will happen if she is guilty?\" asked Dorothy.\r","\r","\"She must die,\" answered the Princess.\r","\r","\"Nine times?\" enquired the Scarecrow.\r","\r","\"As many times as is necessary,\" was the reply. \"I will ask the Tin\r","Woodman to defend the prisoner, because he has such a kind heart I am\r","sure he will do his best to save her. And the Woggle-Bug shall be the\r","Public Accuser, because he is so learned that no one can deceive him.\"\r","\r","\"Who will be the jury?\" asked the Tin Woodman.\r","\r","[Illustration: PORTRAIT OF THE WIZARD OF OZ.]\r","\r","\"There ought to be several animals on the jury,\" said Ozma, \"because\r","animals understand each other better than we people understand them.\r","So the jury shall consist of the Cowardly Lion, the Hungry Tiger, Jim\r","the Cab-horse, the Yellow Hen, the Scarecrow, the Wizard, Tik-tok the\r","Machine Man, the Sawhorse and Zeb of Hugson's Ranch. That makes the nine\r","which the law requires, and all my people shall be admitted to hear the\r","testimony.\"\r","\r","They now separated to prepare for the sad ceremony; for whenever an\r","appeal is made to law sorrow is almost certain to follow--even in a\r","fairyland like Oz. But it must be stated that the people of that Land\r","were generally so well-behaved that there was not a single lawyer\r","amongst them, and it had been years since any Ruler had sat in judgment\r","upon an offender of the law. The crime of murder being the most dreadful\r","crime of all, tremendous excitement prevailed in the Emerald City when\r","the news of Eureka's arrest and trial became known.\r","\r","The Wizard, when he returned to his own room, was exceedingly\r","thoughtful. He had no doubt Eureka had eaten his piglet, but he realized\r","that a kitten cannot be depended upon at all times to act properly,\r","since its nature is to destroy small animals and even birds for food,\r","and the tame cat that we keep in our houses today is descended from the\r","wild cat of the jungle--a very ferocious creature, indeed. The Wizard\r","knew that if Dorothy's pet was found guilty and condemned to death the\r","little girl would be made very unhappy; so, although he grieved over the\r","piglet's sad fate as much as any of them, he resolved to save Eureka's\r","life.\r","\r","Sending for the Tin Woodman the Wizard took him into a corner and\r","whispered:\r","\r","\"My friend, it is your duty to defend the white kitten and try to save\r","her, but I fear you will fail because Eureka has long wished to eat a\r","piglet, to my certain knowledge, and my opinion is that she has been\r","unable to resist the temptation. Yet her disgrace and death would not\r","bring back the piglet, but only serve to make Dorothy unhappy.
